O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear son, I have completed this book for you which is the end of the science of medicine along with its explanation, and I have made the end by its expositions and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I will complete this for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is confined in our region and is foreign to all things everywhere, the science has perished and decayed, and nothing remains of it except small descriptions in books by the ancients that the hands have corrupted.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from these (things) has come error and vanity, and intentions have been closed and knowledge has been alienated.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	 It seems to me that I should revive it along with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition, declaration and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	 And I will come together with the forms of iron cauteries and other instruments of work along with the alignment of the declaration and preparation of them as necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has become distant.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And one who engages in this must be well-versed in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, to know the function of the limbs, their forms and connections and separations of them; and have knowledge of bones and nerves and marrow and the number of joints, and the movement and resting places, and the direction of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	 And for this reason Hippocrates said that the name is not much, but with the work it is enough.
et meismement en l’art de main.	 Indeed, in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	 We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the matters stated, should take care to avoid making errors and not harm people.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	 as I have often wished for those who engage in this science, that they abandon their ignorance and lack of experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	 For I saw a mad man who cut an abscess of scrofula or a woman's neck, and he cut the arteries of her neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	 because so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	 And I saw another madman who pulled an arrow from an old man's side, and the arrow was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	 he took a piece of the bladder with it, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had been called to treat him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they cut it out he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	 And I saw another madman who treated the Duke of our land who had a broken leg and with the breakage had a wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	 and the ignorant madman tightened the break above the wound with strong splints, and did not allow any callus to form on the wound, but allowed it to end in this way.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	 And command that he does not dislocate [it] at all;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	 and holds it until the leg is completely swollen and the feet come to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	 I am called to come to him, and I hastened to come to dislocate his leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	 And when I had dislocated it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	 But any corruption of the member is already confirmed and cannot be cured;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	 And the corruption does not cease to spread through the member until all the member is completely destroyed.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And a second eye, or other mirror, which collapses an abscess and then heats it through the malice of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a boil, when it is filled with black bile, one should not touch it with iron unless it is in such a position that all the corrupted matter can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	 And because of this, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	 meaning, labor where there is danger in many positions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	 And I will show in every place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	 Therefore it is necessary that you take care so that the foolish do not speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	 Take your weapons in your scabbard, and take care of your patients gently and firmly, and use the best way possible by the grace of God so that you may be saved and praised.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	 And leave incurable diseases with great regret.
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	 And remove your weapons from that which causes doubt and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	 Galen said in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	 "Do not take care of bad disease, lest you be called a foolish healer.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	 "I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	 The first chapters are about fire cauteries and removing the cautery of ague, and these chapters are ordered from the head to the feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	 and about the shapes of instruments, and about metal objects for cautery, and all that is necessary in work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	 The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and about blisters and wounds, and about the extraction of arrows, and similar things.
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	 and these chapters are ordered and show the shapes of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	 The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things.
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	 And it is ordered from the head down to the feet, and the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Furthermore, as we remember the work, it is necessary that I tell you the quality of the aid and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	 I say that the qualities of the aid, and the harm, are the longest words and most subtle science and secret responses.
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	 and about this they spoke often by the wise ones, and agreed on this;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	 And I believe little of their words, for I doubt their length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	 I say that fire aid is universally used in every constitution where there is matter, regardless of the constitutions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	 This means hot constitution with matter and dry constitution with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	 In the hot and dry constitution together with matter, some spoke and said that fire aid is great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	 And others say the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	 that fire cautery is not good for sickness caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	 For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to cure a hot disease with heat or dryness.
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	 and he who said the opposite stated that fire provides great aid for a hot and dry illness that comes in men's chest.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you understand the body of man and its moisture according to the nature of fire, you will find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it occasionally by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	 And in every way, do not interfere unless those who have tested it and know through long experience the chapter on cauteries, and the diversity of men's complexions, and their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and the outcomes and timing of their ailments.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	 we have no fear of others' complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all mirrors agreed and conformed to the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cautery combined with fire is one of the secrets of cure, and of greater benefit than cautery of burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come outside the member being cooked, and harms no other member unless named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	 Burning medications come from one limb to another while aligning them, and bring diseases of severe healing to the affected limb.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	 ...and possibly kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	 The fire for its intensity and goodness of its substance does not do this if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	 I have found this to be true through experience and the length of my service and study in the art, and it is above the truth of things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	 And so I excuse myself for the length of the speech, because I do not wish to deprive you of the secret that is reserved regarding fire, and the quality of the work, how it battles diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	 Receive [it] in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	Know, son, that they agreed on when cauterizations should be done and chose companions.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	 And I say that cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harm happening beneath is brought to light by the aid of cautery.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	 And especially when cauterization is necessary for immediate relief, except when a greater harm cannot be delayed to come upon the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	 Do not think this way, dear son, as foolish men do.
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	 for the disease which is cured by cautery has no return.
et il le dient ensi;	 and they say this.
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	 But it is not as they think, because cautery is not a remedy that changes the complexion, and dries up the humors causing pain; rather, it is more effective than medicine in terms of its speed of action and the virtue of its work and dominion.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	 And it is possible that the disease sometimes comes according to the constitution of the patient and the nature of the disease and its properties;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	 and are accumulated in him the superfluidities by the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cauteries are administered where there is little superfluity and moisture, as cauterization for pain and similar things, and such pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	 but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	 And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the rear of medicine, and that is so;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	 But they do not believe that cauteries are valuable after medicine, but their intentions are false, and cauteries are the rear of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment for any disease, and they are ineffective, then we administer the cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is worth noting that cauteries are at the rear of medicine, not as the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	 The ancients said that cauteries made of gold are more pliable than those made of iron, and they did not say this for any reason other than the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	 and they said that the lead of the cautery does not cause putrefaction, but this is not always true as I have proven, and found it to be true in some men.
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	 and gold cauteries are more pliable than iron ones, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	 And even when you heat an instrument of gold, you cannot be sure whether it is hot enough by the color of the gold, and it can suddenly cool.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	 and if it is overheated.
si font au feu;	 it melts in the fire.
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	 And thus it has enough obstruction.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use fire cautery, which has been prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have ordered you this chapter on the head from neck to feet, because the veins will be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is effective for both moist and cold conditions of the brain, and it can be used to treat a disease called "soda", as well as many humors that descend from the head into the eyes and ears, and for numerous dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and indeed all illnesses caused by coldness such as paralysis, sode (a term for brain swelling), apoplexy, and similar conditions.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	 The shape of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by a soluble medicine cleansing the head 3 or 4 times, according to what the properties and age and accustomed state of the sick person can withstand.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	 Then pour warm water over the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	 And then make the patient sit crosswise between your hands, and place his hands on warm poultices;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	 After that place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	 And where your thumbs meet, if it bleeds, warm up the cautery called "olivar," as follows:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	 And place it on its joint marked with ink, and do so while pushing and pulling your hand little by little in twisting;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	 then straighten your hand abruptly, and realign the joint if you see the bone protruding;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	 and if you do not see it, then continue the cautery until you see the bone as I told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	 after take some silk and put it inside and soft cotton, and place it on the joint, and leave it for three days.
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	 afterwards place a piece of soft cotton in butter.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	 and leave it until the burn is removed.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	 afterwards treat the wound with an ointment called "tetrafarmacon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	 And the ancients said, when the wound is left open longer, it drains more.
et por ce si aide mues.	 and for this reason, it helps to clean more.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said that the part of the bone should be burnt as much as possible with the cautery, and then the burnt area of the bone should be reattached and healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	 And others say that the cautery should be let rest for a long time and pressed as hard as the size of the weal that women put in their eyes because the fluids are expelled more.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	 and the wound should be left open for a long time.
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	 afterwards it must be treated and bound up.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	 And these two methods of cautery do not seem to be good in every case, except for some men who have fear.
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	 and it seems to me that I should let it drain.
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	 For the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to continuous solutions of nature, as we have testified in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	 And in the same way, when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first sign of cautery is more healing and beneficial for me, and from this practice I work to gather salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of old pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	 When chronic and prolonged pain comes in the head, the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochineal" and purge of the head and oils and plasters.
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	 And if they perform the cautery as we have said before, it is not worth it.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	 Take care that the head of the patient is strong and not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	 Then cauterize below that cautery a little as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	 Then cauterize below each ear bone of the head as previously said, and perform a cautery at the site called "vaselz".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	 and it is the place where leeches are placed.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	 Align your hand so you cannot see to the bone.
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	 The patient feels more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak about it later.
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	 The cauteries of the ear bones should be more subtle than those used for the middle part of the head, and this is their shape:
dou cautere dou chief	In the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	 When pain suddenly arises in one part of the head and the disease extends to the eye, and the eyes are purged with medicines, and other treatments as I have said in the division of diseases have been performed, but it does not help at all.
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	 Then one performs cauterization according to two ways, namely with medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	 The cauterization with medicine is that you take an alum stone, strip the bark and place it on the affected area, and then make a small incision where the pain is located in such a way that you can place the alum stone under the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	 And when it is put back in place, if it is held well and left for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	 Then untie it and apply strong garlic oil to the wound, and leave the wound for two or three days.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	 then put a linen cloth soaked in butter on it as long as it can stay there.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	 After the ointment has healed.
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	 And if you want, do as I have written in some treatises on medicines that burn or the tenth treatment of medicines that burn.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	 The fire cautery should be done as follows.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Heat the cauterization implement with the form given here:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	 It is called "closed" because the head is shaped like a small box or barrel.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	 and put it on the painful place, hold your hand and turn the fire a little bit lightly, until half of the coal's thickness is burned.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	 And lift your hand so that the arteries do not burn, which are outside, and let a plentiful flow of blood come out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	 Put cotton on it with linen, and place it on the affected area for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then put dampened cotton in butter, and then treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	 And if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare", at the tip, be careful not to cover the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	Of emigraine (This line is difficult to translate with certainty due to its archaic language and potential abbreviations. A possible translation could be "from migraines" or "about migraines", but it's not entirely clear from the given text.)
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	 When treating migraines as we have previously said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauteries before mentioned do not suit this medicine or iron, then you must heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	 And in the same manner, on a line half a thumb's length deep, remove your hand once, and hold so as not to cut the artery and not reach the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	 And guard the jawbone that is closed when eating, and let the nerves have no sight but the closed one and let spasms not come to the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or cutting with great fear, especially to him who does not know, and who is not learned and experienced;
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	 let the work proceed in its way;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	 but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it is found in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 And if you see that this cautery does not alleviate the disease and the patient is suffering, cauterize it in the same way as we have said, and heal the wound until it heals.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	 If you see an artery to extract, follow the instructions for the extraction of the artery with a cautery having two blades.
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	 And this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	Of the pain of the ears due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ear due to coldness does not improve with medications and other treatments as we have said in the division, and it persists, then heat this cautery which is called "poins", here is its form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	 After puncturing all around the sick ear, or around both sides where the pain is located, move away a little from the root of the ear once you have marked the location.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	 and have ten pricks around each ear.
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After curing the shoulder when it is healthy.
de la torture de la bouche	Torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	 The torture to be cured by fire is not for those that move due to fever, as we have said in the divisions of disease.
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	 And do not perform cautery on similar cases coming from scorch and from nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	 When you cure this kind of torture that moves due to fever of the eyes and purges of the head and throat gargling, it is not worthwhile, therefore you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	 One in the root of the ear, and another a little distance from the temple, and the third in the corner of the two lips.
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	 and place the cautery in the part that opens healthy, and make it cauterize towards the head of the ear a little below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as one finger.
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	 And let the cautery remain as long as half of the coal is burned;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	 And its resemblance is like the surgeon's instrument that we have mentioned before, but it is slightly more subtle and the blade should be a bit larger.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After healing the wound as I have said before, let it be healed completely.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	 If apoplexy is old and you cure it as we have said, but it does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then perform four cauterizations.
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	 Two above the two forehead bones, one at the neck, and one in the place called "wounds," as we have said before, and the last cauterization on the mouth of the stomach.
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	 And treat as we have said before.
de litargie	The bed for the paralytic.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	 To this disease, you should give the patient large years and round pills made from the brain.
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	 After cutting off the head of the patient entirely, place the mustard plaster on the occiput which is written or treated with mustard plasters.
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	 And this is the method for the cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	 If you do as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	 If he [the patient] urinates in a good manner, it is well;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	 and if he does not, you should perform three cauterizations on the head, descending from the neck to the throat, leaving a space of one finger's width between each.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	 and treat as others do, and if you see it necessary, and the patient is strong enough, perform a cauterization in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if necessary, it is to be placed between the two horns, and it is to be cured until it heals;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	 and let the fire cautery, which is called "olivare", be as I have previously stated.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	 The head should be cleansed for years and as we have previously said;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	 After the reign of the patient's head, then make the cautery in the head and on each horn, and twice on the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	 and if you have further need, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is outside, make four cauteries on the spine of the back;

de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use fire cauteries except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is first necessary to cleanse the brain with years and other treatments as we have said in the division when the patient is great and suffering from taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	 And if it's an infant who cannot tolerate it, give a gargle and chew soft foods frequently with good meats.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	 After the king's head has been boiled, apply the cautery as we have said before on the head and on each horn.
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 If the patient is strong and enduring, apply cautery as I said to someone with paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and the neck, and let it be the "olivier" cautery as I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, apply a subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy are the superfluidities or corrupt and swollen fluids, then cauterize with such cauteries as we have said for those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the cause of melancholy is the superfluity declining towards melancholy, and the body of the sick person is moist, then give them to drink something by which the brain may be purified, according to what has been said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	 After the king (or head) of the patient.
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	 Make a sling from linen well made, like a circle, place it around the head (or neck).
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	 and cross the patient over himself, holding him tightly from all sides.
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	 Then apply the linen bandage, using old goat's butter.
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	 Heat it moderately, so that it is hot enough to be pressed onto him without causing pain.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	 After emptying the circle inside the head (or neck), let it cool.
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Do this to the patient every week with good government, until he is well.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	 Or, if you wish to cauterize someone, make multiple pricks all over the cauterization implement.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	 This method of cautery reduces (or relieves) the skull greatly.
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	 And then place cotton wool moistened with butter and linseed oil on it.
de l’awe des eulz	Of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eyes begin to come first through the signs that I have said in the division, then commence and give the patient something purifying the head, and keep it away from all moisture, and make him sweat or take a bath several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	 Then tell him to lie down on his back, and make a fire-cautery in the head, and make two more cauteries on both temples where the defect of the eye or the eyes is, or one defect is in one.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	 And apply the entire cautery to all veins and arteries that are beneath the skull, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple.
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	 And beware of the discharge of blood, and if you see too much blood flowing out, stop it with your power as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	 And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in making incisions with caution, how to stop it.
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	 And sometimes they make a cautery or a hot iron under the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	The tears of the body
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	 When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are above the veins or have been removed from the arteries that are in the appearance of the forehead;

et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	 If necessary, also cauterize carefully above the eyelid with small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	The tears of the body within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	 When the medicine, as we have said in the division, does not work, then give the patient three warm cocktails.

Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And here is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	 When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then perform the cauterization using this implement called "olivar.
de coi ci est li forme:	 This is the form (of the procedure):
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	 If you wish to perform this fire cautery on the two warts as long as they are, like serpents;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 and do not leave the hand except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that pricks the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	 Sometimes the hair of the eyes is converted into a gland and pricks the oil, and then one performs a fire cautery according to these two methods;
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	 it means by fire or burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	 For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	 and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	 When they are born and even, then put the patient in a healthy state.
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	 On top of the paper, draw a figure similar to the fennel seed cluster and mark the beginning of the sign along the hairs.
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Then put moistened cotton in egg white and ground pepper oil on it, then heat the fire cautery of this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	 Cauterize at the figure you have marked several times, until the edge is burned.
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	 And the signs of the operation's health are that you see the paper recede and the hairs lift at the oil's tip.

aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the ointment treatment until it heals.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	 And when hairs appear, and the paper is softened then start the cautery on that same spot again, as you did first.

Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	 The medical cauterization is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a paper in the shape of the myrtle leaf.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	 Then take French soap and quicklime, one ounce each and grind them together well.
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	 And make it quickly, so as not to cool it; then place the paper over the eyes.
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	 and if the patient holds it only in one eye, it should be treated in that one; and if in both, in both as well.
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	 and put cotton soaked in egg white under the eye.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	 The patient's shoulder should be in a good position and place your hand on the medicine showing upwards, and press the thumb and move it every time the patient feels the bite of the medicine, because it bites as much as fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a while, remove the medicine from your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	 And when the bite has passed, raise the shoulder and look to see if the paper is raised as it was by the constraint of fire or by an incision.
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	 And if it is thus, it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	 If that is not the case, reset the medicine on the place or the medicine has not worked yet, as long as your efforts are equal and your eyes placed correctly;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then put cotton wadded in butter on it until the wound heats up, afterwards cure the place of the ointment called "diaphanis" and other ones, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	 And if you need to be careful about your work, keep a great distance from the eyes so that no medicine drips onto them.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	 And if the paper becomes soft afterwards and the hairs prick in the oil, start the treatment again on that place which was made soft by the paper properly, just as you did before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Afterwards cure it until it is healed.
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	 And this is the shape of the fennel seed.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	 Know that human eyes are diverse in size and smallness, according to your constraints;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	 And the straight path should not be replied to him who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When treating a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases and your treatments do not help, then you must perform cautery on it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	 Instruct the patient to put his head in your lap;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	 And the assistant should grasp the patient's head between his hands in such a manner that it does not move or lower its head.
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	 Then place cotton wool soaked in egg white or linseed oil on top of it.
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	 After heating the iron branding tool that is metal.
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	 And press it against the head like the shape of a plumb bob, with the hot iron branding tool at the same time;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	 If it is seen, let it be pointed from one head to the other, and if it is seen, let it also be like a tent.
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	 However, this which is placed at the head is moved for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	 After you have compressed the fistula if it is open, and drain out the pus, then dry it.
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	 And if it is closed, open it, and draw out the pus forcefully;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	 Then place the hot iron cautery on it, and hold your hand on the cautery at the base of the nail so that your hands do not move.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	 And put the cautery in the oil fat, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	 If you come at the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	 If that does not work, repeat the cautery again if you need to, and leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	 Afterward place cotton wool dipped in butter on it, and the ointment of the desiccative cure until it is dry, and if forty days pass and it is not dry, put on a corrosive medicine while the bone is exposed.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	 And the king in accordance with what he will come to write in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	 And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula which none of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	 Make an opening for the fistula and cut into it;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	 Afterwards put in the fissure the camel's hair fine as this is its shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	 and they fill it with the quantity of a half-pound of pitch.
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	 Hold your hand firmly on the camel's hair, and let the patient not move at all, until the pitch melts over its oil.
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	 And it is necessary to anoint the patient's affected area with oil and soft cotton dipped in egg yolk or almond oil.
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	 The flesh should be cut open where there is a fistula, and the pus drawn off by a marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	 And if the fistula has been healed by the cautery we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	 If it's not healed, then administer pepper to the newborn, and bring the fistula back into the newborn's body as appropriate in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	cavities in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there appear cavities in lips, which are called "hair," and also in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cavities as we have said in the previous section, and the treatment does not help, then boil a small cautery knife using this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	 And apply it immediately into those cavities until it reaches the source.
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After treating the wound with cerote (medieval antiseptic) until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess in the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	 When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or eye, or nose, or teeth roots, after pus production and swelling and becomes a fistula.
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	 And you cure it as we have said in the previous section, but it does not improve.
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	 Then it is necessary to use cautery according to the size of the fistula.
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	 After the blow or loss of the fistula, hold your hand until the iron is hot at its source and at its base.
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And do this once or twice, after treating what we have said in treatments, until it is healed.
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	 and if it is healed thusly, it is good.
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	 And if not, you must discover the source and remove the corrupt bone, as you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	The movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	 When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicine but it is of no use, then put the head of the patient on your lap.
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	 After heating the cautery as will be shown later in this manner: you place a cane on the tooth.
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	 Place the hot cautery inside [the affected area] as quickly as possible, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat approaching the root of the tooth.
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	 After leaving your hand, continue with the cautery according to your will.
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	 Fill the patient's mouth with saltwater and keep it there for an hour and a half.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the moving tooth is confirmed, and the softened gums are held tight, and the corrupt moisture dries up.
de la dolor des dens	From the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	 If dental pain comes from cold or there is cold or fever, and the medical cures do not work, then it is necessary to use cautery according to two methods:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	 and the cauterization with butter and the cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	 The cauterization with butter is as follows: take butter from a cow and mold it into the shape of an iron spoon or ladle.
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	 After taking cotton and wrapping it on the tip of a tent, and moistening it in bull's bile, place it quickly on the painful tooth and hold it until it is cooled.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	 And do this often until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see the cotton and linen moistened in cold bile, place it on the swollen tooth, and put the hot iron on it until the heat reaches the root of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	 The cautery with fire is such that you take a thick iron or steel cane, and it should be large enough so that the heat does not reach the patient's mouth.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	 After heating the cautery, wait for its shape to come after it, and place it on the tooth, holding your hand until the cautery is cooled.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	 Do this often, for the pain will disappear from that day itself or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	 And it is necessary that the patient fill their mouth with good butter in the urgency of this cautery, and then blow hard.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	 And make a cauterization at the head that you wish, and according to what you are able.
et c’est li forme de la caine:	 And this is the form of the cane:
des scrophules	of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	 When scrophulas are of fluid and cold moisture, and do not obey digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery as described below, and have it open so that the smoke can exit to the other side of the cauterization.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	 And place the hot fire cautery on the abscess once, where it is needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	 And if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it like that for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	 and place moist cotton on it with butter until the pus is expelled;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the wound has been cured with ointments and plasters, make sure it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	 The form of the arm:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	 When moisture prevails over the channels of the intestine, and especially when it comes from a cold constitution, then the patient must be purged first with soluble medicines;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	 After the cautery is applied to the root of the throat, be careful not to approach the throat, and do it with caution but only a little bit;
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	 Afterwards, perform the other cautery at the joint of the neck at the spine's head, and it is the cautery that is called "clavicle," as we have its shape beforehand.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and heal the joint as we have said before until it is healthy.
de la toust	The tooth
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	 When all and disease of parmon are from cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or scorching, and it is an old disease, perform two cauteries on the swelling in visible joints.
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	 And another cautery in the worst area between the two breasts.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	 And it is the cautery called "clavicle," according to the shape that has been said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	 And if you see, perform cautery by pricking with the entire cautery called "point" as its shape is described in the disease of ears.
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	 And let the tips be up to 30 [degrees], or around [them].
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	 After curing the joint as stated before, let the cautery be at three intervals according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because these cauteries are lighter, because you make them in two applications (copies).
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	 Afterwards let the patient lay down on their back and side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	 afterwards, take hold of the curved part with your left hand thumb;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	 and if the joint is dislocated internally, cauterize it using the double pronged instrument that has this shape here:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	 and cauterize the wound until it pierces the chest cavity, causing the figure of the cautery to come together with four cauteries;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	 and this is done by using a three-pronged cautery because the figure of the cauterization consists of several cauteries;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	 and the nerves are arranged according to the subtlety of a tent and this is the shape of the three-pronged cautery;
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes, it is tied on top of this nerve, for which there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	 After place the cautery over it, grind with ashes.
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	 After placing the patient, let not the limbs be moved for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 If it is dislocated above, which happens seldom, then perform cautery above the thick part of the cauterizing iron, or many cauteries in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When in the stomach there are coldness and much moisture which bring it to its constitution, and many catarrhs come upon him, and in the ways of treatment customary for him, it does not help; therefore, the patient should be made to lie down on his back, and extend his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	 After that, make three cauterizations beneath the spoon-shaped depression in the amount of one finger width, on all parts of the cautery, and two cauterizations outside the two sides so that the figure of the cauteries is at three angles, and leave enough space between one and another so they are not joined together when they release pus.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 and the cauterizations should be so deep that they pierce the two parts of the wound, and the figure of the cauteries according to this form without deviation:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	 And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery within the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	 and he who has fear of the cautery, cauterize by pressing and holding on the stomach at the point according to the quantity that you wish.
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 then cauterize all the cautery which is called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the healing of the wound has occurred, when it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	 When it comes to the liver, there is pain from cold and moisture and a great windiness, until it is removed from its natural composition due to excesses.
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	 and the patient is cured of what we have said in the previous sections, but it does not help him at all, it is necessary that the patient be conscious on his bed.
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	 and make three cauterizations according to this form, this shape, and this quantity on the liver, pushing aside the hypochondria, where the ribs of the man come.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	 And let there be space between each cautery, the thickness of two fingers.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	 Let the cauterization be long enough to accommodate a finger and do not press too much with your hand on all the cautery.
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	 And only burn the middle part (of the wound) and let the patient be upright on his feet;
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	 And if he cannot stand, he should lie down, extend his legs, and raise his arms.
et c’est li forme:	 That is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	 If your desire is to perform these cauteries with a scalpel, be careful and cautious in the art, and do not burn all the way through, because you will scorch the entire body.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And let it not go up to the boiling point, because the core is very subtle there, and the wise one can see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	 When there is an abscess in the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	 if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not very strong;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 and if it is in the membrane, he feels insane pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	 And when this cure ends, it is necessary that the patient be conscious of his head.
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 and then press on the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a plowshare, such as this is its shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	 Heat the cautery until the blades are hot, and come to a boil, so that the pus is completely expelled.
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	 after the cure according to the cure for swellings, until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 It is not advisable to use this fire cautery by anyone who has not studied the art of medicine for a long time, as these diseases have been aggravated on many occasions by it.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	 Then it can be boldly operated, but I think it is worth leaving it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	 The ancients said that plasters made from the roots of Aristolochia should be applied in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	 Take a long root of Aristolochia, the largest one you can find, and let it be dry, as large and as long as your thumb.
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	 and moisten it in oil, heat it, and apply the fire cautery between the armpit and the neck, and place small cauteries a little lower in the area below the beard.
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	 and the cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, sloping slightly back.
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	 And the incision into the worst part, and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and the two ribs outward from the incision between the shoulders.
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	 And do not press your hand, but make it open in the same way as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	 And some old man said that anyone uses a cautery resembling a razor, and they heat it up and place it between the ribs until it reaches an abscess.
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	 And he jumps beyond the pain, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	 But in this work, there is fear or the patient dies immediately, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse (as we have said in the divisions of cures), and it does not help, then apply three methods of cauterization, all of which are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	 Of which one method is that you make three or four incisions, in a line following the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the liver cautery we have said before.
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	 And after that do not rush your hand with all the cautery, let the patient be aware on his back.
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	 And another way of cauterizing is that you heat the cautery with two nerves, as we have shown in the shoulder dislocation.
et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	 and lift the incision that is towards the mouse, where the patient's pain comes from on the left side, and raise the elevations as you make the incision according to the length of the body, and the cautery should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII.	 After that put the two nerves into the flame until they are heated and pierced from the other side, then pull out the cautery, and thus there will be four [pieces].
