Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	 In small wounds, use what is appropriate, then take the minister who has anointed all the wound with his hand and press the lips together.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	 and this is the common method of stitching, and you should take one needle or more, according to the size of the wound's width, then leave some space from the edge of the wound, and sew with a strong threaded needle.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	 and pierce the two shoulders of the skin with the two needles that are beneath the skin from this side, until you make a hole through that part, and join the four edges of the skin together.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	 then tighten a double thread around the needle from both sides, then join the two edges of the wound together, and leave some space, and sew another stitch.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	 then tie the thread as you did with the first stitch, and do not stop making these stitches according to how many stitches are needed, until the entire wound is closed.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	 And let the needles be of medium size, neither too fine nor too coarse; for fine needles pierce all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot enter well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	 because they should be of medium size;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	 and it is not good to insert the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they pierce and open the wound before the suture.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	 and then bend the heads of the needles so they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and place stoppers or cloth on the heads of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is sutured.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	 and this way of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, since it requires only one needle.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	 The second suture is common, and it consists of joining the two shoulder blades and the two breastbones together with a needle that has a strong medium thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	 and when you have pierced all four of the bones together, remove the needle from the part where you began, in the manner one does with linen.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	 and put some space between each suture using the thickness of a small egg.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 This suture was done to a man, and I sewed up a wound that a knight had on his stomach which was cut by a knife, and the wound was more than one palm wide, and it exposed the intestines by two palms, and the wound was inside the stomach.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I brought back the intestine after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was sewn up for 15 days, healed, and became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	 And they had judged him to be dying, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	 and did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where none were found, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 and put cotton old twice a day on the wound, and washed it with water of honey until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	 Now I shall tell you the two proper ways of sewing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	 take the needle and thread from the outer part all the way to the inner side;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	 when it has pierced the skin straight through, if the end of the seam or stitch where you put the needle, and make it pierce from the inner side all the way to the outer side;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 And the understanding of this stitching is that you sew it as furriers sew fur, and that you leave one opening at a time, and close it from the other side, until the stitching is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	 The second way of stitching, which Galen calls specifically, is like anyone who brings together two parts naturally, and applies one end of the seam to the other end in such a manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	 insert a needle or point of the mirror nearby, and pierce only that place, and leave the two ends of the seam;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	 then turn the needle and pierce from the outside to that inside, through the two ends of the seam;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	 Then pierce one and the other from the outer part up until inside, in the two shoulders that are on the opposite sides.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 and this is the twisted manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	 Galen said this word, and no one denies it, one should sew the abdomen with two needles, or have thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	 and one must insert one needle from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew leather.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 And know that when the wound is within the abdomen, the stitching is more difficult than in other parts of the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	 The judgement of a wound is such as the judgement of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	 And when you find the fresh wound full of blood, as soon as the arrow has moved it, then reset the intestines and stitch (it).
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	 Then put the warming charcoal powder on it, and if the arrow has moved it, then put any available ointment on it until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	 and sew the threads together, and the ligature (sifac) and miret (a type of dressing).
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then treat the wound as others do, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 If you don't have medicine, put old cotton on it as soon as it begins to heal, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	 You have no need for other medicine in most cases where the wounds are simple.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	 and if you doubt that the wound will infect the main members, then you must dampen light linen in warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the joints, and under the buttocks.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	 and if it causes pain or putrefaction in the belly, which often occurs, then cleansing with black wine can help, and especially when the putrefaction reaches the intestines.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 and pierce it from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The "youthful" intestine cannot heal when it is perforated, and this is due to the inflammation of veins that are present there, and due to the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	 And if the worm jumps out of the wound, put it back in the same way as the intestine, while it is still fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	 And if it is old and turned black or dark, you should cut away the black part where blood does not come out, because there are veins and arteries there.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 Then cut out what is between the ligament, and hang the two heads suspended from the part beneath the wound to align the extraction when the flesh falls off, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bladder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	 When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, because I have seen that a man was pierced or stabbed with a spear through his stomach.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	 And the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became a hernia and turned into a fistula, and in it was the excretion and wind.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 I treat him according to what I know, and I did not stop refining until he was healthy, and the bones were healed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	 And when I saw the bones heal, I feared that the patient might have something wrong in his stomach.
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	 But he had no ill, but stayed in better condition, and dieted and drank.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	 And the experimentalists said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	 Take large forceps, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the forceps have opened the mouth, place it on the two lips so that it stretches the mouth.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	 And then hold the head and keep it so that it cannot be released, then place another forceps after in this manner as before until the wound is completely seized.
et cout la plaie.	 And dress the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	 If the head adheres in the intestine and causes no harm to the patient, it can be tied with a thin thread made from the intestine of an animal in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	 take the head of this thread from intestine and make it smooth, then tie it to the head of a thin linen thread in a twist, then insert the thread into the needle, sew the intestine and draw out the suture.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	 and this method of stitching hernias is not without fear and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 If the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no help or healing, but only subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of a fistula or when it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it develops, is universally called "fistula", and likewise when it opens up and becomes hollow.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	 And a fistula is similar to a hard, white nodule that does not cause pain, and it is as hollow as the quill of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	 and sometimes clear and loose, and other times firm.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	 Sometimes narrow, and other times wide.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	 And I have spoken of it in the section on wounds, that any wound which is not healed and there is no flesh, this is not without one of the nine causes.
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	 This means: by smallness of blood or body.
ou por sa malice;	 Or by its corruption.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	 Or because there is hard flesh within and above the lips that does not allow new flesh to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	 Or it has too much pus.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	 When the joint is dislocated, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	 and the medicine is not good in treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	 because corruption is a kind of plague.
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	 because in the region, digestion is slow, health slows down, and it swells by nature.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	 or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 and I have already shown all these causes, the signs, and the remedies of medicines in the divisions.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I must tell you the remedy for a fistula made by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	 Know that fistula occurs in all the limbs of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	 because there are fistulas that come from the large veins, arteries, nerves, or the intestines, bladder, ribs, spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet.
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 And if it comes to the property of the main member or similar joints.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	 All these fistulas of this kind are of grave healing, and there is but labor and ignorance in it.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	 And if there is any fistula which does not come up to the level that I have said, and you are confident of its cure, and you know it, then take a tent of linen or iron, if the fistula is straight, and sew it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	 And if the fistula is twisted, then search for a thin tent of lead, because lead bends with the twist.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	 And if the fistula has many holes and you cannot search for it with tents, then clisterize (cleanse) it through one of the holes, because moisture is short from one hole to another, and clean it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	 Then feel carefully with your power if there is bone or nerve, and if it is broken in full, ask the patient clearly about the pain they feel when pressed by your hand, and where they feel it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	 and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint or nerve or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I told you, if the fracture is transverse, then cut off the damaged and corrupted parts within.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	 and then cure it as long as it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply draining in the right place, then you should cut it through completely, as much as possible, then put dampened tents filled with hot medicine into it, and push them to the top of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And then apply salve unguents on the affected healthy flesh, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And if it is not healed by this means, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupt from the fistula, strike it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	 If a vein or nerve does not hinder or affect the main limbs as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, strike it until all corruption is removed, then apply salve unguents until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	 And if it is not healed and it breaks again as before, know that you are not going to the fountain:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	 expose and cut until you reach the bottom, remove all corruption, then restore the joint.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 And if it [the shoulder] is thus healthy, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	 And if it [the shoulder] isn't like that, know that the corruption is too advanced, so you cannot fix it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	 if there is no other remedy but to let it rest by nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	 and if there is a little corrupted bone and you can extract it with pliers, take it out if the instrument is suitable for that, and if there are multiple bones, take them all out, do not leave any one of them.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 And if the moisture opposes you and there is no mistake or fear, press and heat and bandage the wound, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	 And if you cannot remove the bones within an hour, put something irritating pus on the wound and leave it until the flesh grows around the bones, and then the bones will be easier to remove.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	 And if it is a large bone, like the leg or thigh, you should only cauterize the decay until all the blackness has been burned off, then heal the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	 and if there is extensive decay, reaching down to the bone.
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	 it must be cauterized and covered up to the decay, then healed until it is closed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And I will tell you about a fistula that occurs in the leg near the joint, so you can take it as an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	 There was a young man around 30 years old who had pain in his leg from an internal cause causing matter to come to the leg, and he developed a large abscess that could not be opened.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	 But the fools with their folly overdid it so that the abscesses opened up, and they became filled with matter, and it turned into a fistula, and much pus came out which caused the body to be full of wetness.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	 and they applied many remedies for two years without any skilled hand in the art of medicine, as long as I was called upon, and I saw his leg and the medicines they used to treat him, and it ran pus with great swelling.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 And the youth's body became red, and he had a citron-colored complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I inserted a tent (stitch) in one of the wounds, and then I searched all the wounds, and found that some were coming towards the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	 So I hurried and inserted into one of the sores until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came up to the bone within.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	 I appeared to me that the bone was corrupt, and I thought there was no other corruption except that which I left.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	 And I began to treat the wound with salty medicines for a long time, but it could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	 Then I began again, and opened the bone as before, and found that the corruption was continuous in the bone, and I removed it, and then left it alone, and tried to heal the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	 But I could not even cover a palm of the bone, and it was torn away entirely, then I treated it with medicines.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 And it was healed and strengthened quickly, and there was no need to begin the work again except due to the weakness of the patient who could not endure, and due to my fear of death for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 Because of the blood evacuation, it often became healthy entirely, and grew in the bone a hard cyst, and was of good condition and had no harm or contrary effect in any way, neither at its side nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	 And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, it must be treated in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	 Take a splint and bind it to the open end of the broken bone, and instruct someone to pull it upwards:
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	 and place another thicker bandage over the first one, bind it above the skin away from the bone, and pull the rotten flesh downwards to expose the healthy skin where you want it to be, so that the new skin does not puncture the old:
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	 and place fire or a hot iron under the bone to heat the rotten flesh:
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 it is necessary to be patient until one can see and feel the rottenness has subsided, and be patient yet again:
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	 And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or a part of it, uncover all the flesh.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	 Then place the iron under it, and then sew from one part to another the corruption, and let the iron tip be as long as the length of the corruption, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	 And if the corruption is in the joint, strike the corrupted joint, and let the bone be from the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	 and if the corruption is between two joints, there is no remedy but to cover it.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	 And if the corruption is at the knuckle of the hand or foot, it is a very serious matter, but nevertheless you must investigate this corruption and how to open it.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	 And clean it in all ways you can, but make sure that the vein or nerve do not oppose you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	 And know that the cutting instruments and saws for covering these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	 And therefore, you should prepare each type of work with its appropriate tool.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	 And know that the work will show you the tool you will need, according to your knowledge of this craft and the signs of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 If you consider the tool that you require according to what is necessary.
dou feu	the fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	 The head may dislocate either from within or due to displacement;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	 and when you have applied the corrosive cure for that corruption using medicines, but it does not help, then it is necessary to cover the affected limb up to the level where the corruption occurs. This way the patient escapes death from this or from the greater evil, which is the defect of the member;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	 and the signs are that the limb turns black, as if it were burnt by fire. Afterwards, blackness spreads from one member to another, gradually taking over the entire body;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 if you hasten to cover [it], and it is due to the bite of certain poisonous animals such as scorpions from the sea, snakes, and similar creatures; if the corruption is at the head of the penis, then cover it, but do not allow space for the venom to reach as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	 And if it reaches up to the hand, strike it at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach as far as the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	 and if it reaches to the elbow, strike it at the bend.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	 and if it passes the bend, it is death, and there is no help but in the quantity of its power.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	 and thus do as when the corruption comes or pierces.
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	 if it comes at the first joint, strike after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	 and if it pierces, strike all the way through.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	 and if it moves into the leg, strike at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	 and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to wear out the patient with pain.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	 And the method for covering or sewing the limb is such that you tie it above and below, and extend one of the strips downward, and another strip upward, and you pull the flesh which is between the two strips apart with a spatula wide enough so that the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 Then cover or sew it with linen on both sides, so that the stitches do not touch the healthy part, and bring other harm to the patient in the form of injury and abscesses.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	 And if bleeding occurs during the operation, cauterize the area immediately or place some powders that restrain it on top.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the limb with a strong cord and heal it until it is healthy.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	 And I will tell you what happens to the man lying there:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	 a man lying there had a blackness that seemed burned by fire, and the rotting began first in his foot, until it took all of the leg.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	 and when the man saw the rotting, he covered his leg with copper, and became clean.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	 A long time later the rotting returned to his hand, and it came to me, and I put him on remedies after cleansing the body, but the rotting could not be stopped.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	 And it is clear to me that I will amputate the hand, for I have no hope of healing the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	 And I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the strength of the man was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	 And he gave up completely, returned to his earth, and struck his hand with a spade, and was healthy;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 I have no knowledge of this story except for the fact that it is told in order to do something else if needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	 An abscess never comes in a charnel house and remains for such a long time that it causes a great gathering of flies;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	 And then they run and pierce and fly away, leaving the place visible, just like a servant;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	 The skin that is on top is as thin as woven fabric that has been torn apart, and it does not penetrate to the bone or to the nerve, and such an illness is called "sain," not "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	 but if it is long enough to reach the bone entirely, it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	 and the care is that you pierce the skin all around, and likewise when it is subtle, as a linen cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 and not for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	 And if you have faith that the skin has become hard and corruption is not in the entirety, and the skin is thick with pus, cure it with clysteris thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	 Look if the breasts are large, and the boils that are in it have a strong smell, then cleanse them with Egyptian medicine made as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	 take aloeswood, oil, and pitch, equal amounts, cook them in a pot over fire until the medicine becomes red and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	 and then take some of this according to your need, make it into water and honey, and cleanse the breast, and apply pressure on the sore.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	 leave the medicine for two hours, then strain it through a cloth;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	 do this several times until the breast is healed and the pus is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	 and occasionally cleanse with water of ashes, when this medicine is not present, and you take vine ash water, pour it on, then let it cool, and apply, until you know that the breast is well cleansed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	 And if the patient cannot endure it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor water of ashes, then let him be cleansed with water and honey or have a small amount of crushed litargyre mixed in it.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	 or cleanse him with honey and sweetened wine, so that the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine strengthens the blood.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	 and when you have done this and you are sure that the breasts have been well cleansed, cleanse them with what causes growth in them, and take a diaphytum root, grind it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	 or cleanse him with various medicines and ointments, as I have said their properties for treating sores.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	 And if the breast ulcer is small and the probe of the cupping glass cannot enter, enlarge it with a bit of iron and put on an Egyptian ointment or basilicon until it is opened.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if the wound is too large, let it heal on its own or allow the cupping glass to enter, and if there is a breast abscess above it, press or lower it more.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	 For when the abscess is full, do not let pus drain.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	 And if you cannot cover the breast with a bandage as desired, arrange it in such a way that the abscess descends to the lowest level possible, for when the abscess is full, do not let pus drain and if you cannot cover the breast with a bandage as desired.
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	 The bow string runs smoothly downwards, and do not let anything slip from the bow.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	 and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and place it on a linen cloth that covers the entire wound.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	 then press the forces towards the wound in a hole larger than the first one, then oint it with oil on another cloth according to the size of the wound, and place it on the wound of the bowel to align it, and do not remove the large cloth until after several days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	 and the one who is on the wound of the intestine, frequently removes it to remove the bowel, and knows what will come out from the bowel, whether it is poison or too much or digested or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	 And take care if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been applied in this manner and you see the nature that rises above the wound pus, then know that the breast will certainly open up, approach the healthy.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 Then loosen it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change another bandage, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	If the breasts are swollen and do not improve after several days, know that they will not swell further.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poisonous worms crawl for a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	 For there are men who delay applying lard in their wounds, and those who do the opposite of this;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	 and if he swallows food improperly from the breast after many days, know that the breast will not open up.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	 If the breast takes a long time to open up and is swollen, apply drying medicines that are moist in substance and dry in effect, as ointment of this kind, for there is great need of vitriol, and it is the last medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	 Take the unguent defined, and make it with rose oil, and mix an equal amount of old wine in substance.
puis le confit et en use;	 Then cook and use it.
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	 and the same thing, cooked more thickened, when the unguent defined is not present, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind it, and powder it on the honey when it is above the fire.
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	 and then apply it to the cloth, and place it on the breast, and sometimes an astrologer long is given, and roots of celestial lily, which is as flour of bread and cinnamon.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	 and use of simple or compound medicines:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	 grind them, make into powder, and put on the honey I said, and use.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	 And if the limb is long and not treated by this cure, then know that corruption has spread throughout it, and causes pressure on the bone or in hard members or ligaments.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 If the treatment for fistula (which we have previously mentioned).
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess at the nailbed
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	 Paranaris is an abscess that arises under the nail of the hand or foot, or by chance it appears in other places.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	 And when it (the abscess) is neglected and no care is taken of it, if the abscess grows, it will spread and run along until it reaches the root of the nail, and possibly all of it.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 And the corruption comes up to the bone, causing a stinky pain, and the toes are large and discolored.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the previous section and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the excess that remains of the nail, followed by cauterizing the wound.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	 The cautery is very helpful if the bone is healthy, and the nail is intact.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	 If the nail penetrates the skin and starts to swell, and begins to point, you should place a reed beneath the nail so it does not pierce the skin, push it upwards, and gently and softly strike the swelling, and apply the remaining char of corrosive and burning medicine to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then heal with ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	 If the corrosion is in the bone, strike and draw out pus, because as the bone becomes more corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 If you see two bones corrupting, strike them with force as mentioned before, then heal until it heals.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	 And if it is wounded, struck, and causes great pain, then you must first let it bleed.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	 Then cut the nail with a sharp spatula from the side and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if it happens, put something on it to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deaf man's hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The patient must cauterise who is born with a growth in some people's hands by chance, which is entirely flesh, and sometimes it has bone, and occasionally it has nail; and one of these never grows from the joint root or the growth emerges from any of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	 The one born inside the egg does not close its mouth, and the one born at the egg joint may or may not close its mouth.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	 The incision of the fleshy one is easy in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	 The one born at the root of the joint is difficult to treat.
si te tien dou coper.	 Keep yourself covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one born or should be in the little finger, it is necessary that you cut round the flesh up to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and treat it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The same sores that come at the joints come together by birth, or by injury of a wound, or by burning with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	 You must suture that wound, so it should repair according to its natural shapes.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	 then put between two tents or damp cloths soaked in rose oil, so they do not adhere.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 Or you put between two thin planks until the flesh is sutured, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	In the same way, if any of his hands comes with the palm, then strike that joint as necessary.
des vils	 of peasants
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	 These are large veins swollen with melancholic fluids that come in many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 And it happens more often in legs of those who walk and work and carry things, rather than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must sometimes administer purge of bile, and then let it flow from the basilica (biliary duct).
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	 The treatment with iron is according to two methods.
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	 one is by striking them and drawing out black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 And another way is to open the vein and pull it all through.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	 The incision is as follows according to this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	 First, the leg is incised deeply with very hot water until the large muscle is softened, then hold the patient's leg above the calf to the part below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	 then cut the vein in one of the three places, with a large incision, and separate it and pull black blood to your hand from one end to another until as much blood comes out as the patient's strength can tolerate.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	 then tie it up and instruct him to bind himself with black vinegar-soaked meat.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 And repeat the evacuation and cleaning when veins are full, it harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	 The swellings of them are according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	 Raise the leg of the patient if it has much hair, then put it in water, and rub the leg with hot water until it turns red, and inflate the veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	 And if you don't have water, heat it with fire, then apply it to the vein along the length of the thigh or in the part below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	 Then scrape the skin with a sharp edge, and peel off the vein from each side, as much as it appears when you feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	 And one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	 Push the probe beneath, as long as it is raised from the skin, and then cut it at an angle, then strike it in another place three inches away.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	 Then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then remove the probe as before, and cut it at another angle as you did before.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	 Then strike another size, or more if needed, then remove it, and strike the tooth at the second incision, then pull it out until the second incision.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	 Then pull it out by size, until it comes out entirely, then strike it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	 And if you cannot draw and lift it, push an awl through its entire length, bind and pull it, and push it under the skin, then turn your hand from one side to another until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	 And be careful that it does not tear, for if it tears, you cannot draw or lift it, and this causes harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	 And when you have treated it all, place on the wound a linen cloth moistened with wine and rose oil.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And keep treating it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	 If the eye is contracted, twisted and rolled together, not straight as we have said, you must cut it carefully but do not cover it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And pull it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	 The shape of the iron used to pierce the vein should be curved and not cut, but should pierce it.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 And is of thick curvature because if it was thin, it would pierce the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the common vein (civil vein)
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	 This vein is located in the legs, in warm areas where no grass or trees grow, and in dry ground.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 And by chance it may appear in places other than the legs, and this happens due to a pustule that comes from under the skin, just as it appears inside the body of snakes and eels, veins appearing between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that a very large inflammation comes in the leg, then the limbs change and the vein begins to burst out like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	 When the shoulder is opened, it is necessary that you wind around a piece of wood from one and a half to two feet long, knot it, and leave the wood by the leg, and every time it comes out, you wind around the wood again and knot it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	 And if it is too long, you chop off a part and wind up the rest, but do not cover it in its root, until it is all out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	 for if you chop it, it will go back into the flesh, causing an abscess and pus or a bad illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	 Therefore, that thing must be treated little by little until the head is reached, and nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	 And sometimes this vein, when treated, becomes of such length, either 5 or 10 fingers, and once a man came to me whose it was 10 fingers in length. When you open it, push the nail or finger against it and pierce through to the end, so that everything comes out;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 and empty the matter that is inside, and bring healing medicinal ointment to it for three days, then treat it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	 And sometimes this vein swells up and more so when it opens at the joint of the foot or leg, and it bleeds profusely and often bursts, causing it to jump.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 Treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	 This disease is called on our land "malady of ox", because it often happens to bulls, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body, expanding and contracting, and it hurts greatly in one member after another until the skin or where it goes breaks open;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	 and it is infested with corruption of some humors, such as worms, snakes, lizards, or roundworms in the abdomen;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	 and there is doubt about its malignancy, because when it goes through the body, it rises to the head, and it may enter the eye, perhaps destroying the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	 and such things happen frequently.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	 When you see him to cure and drain, it can only be done when he goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	 Then you must lie him down on a hard surface with a strong and narrow rope both above and below, then strike above and drain the blood out of it completely, if it empties in full into the flesh, and you cannot stop it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	 and the greatest harm that it does, is that it will cause oil to run, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	 and if you see it coming or close to the oil, hold a bellows under him in form, then strike above, and drain the blood out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 it is necessary for the patient to use a cleansing of the body with soluble medicines to remove evil humors and wash away stinking foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	 This disease is called "vakirir" on our land, and it is a pain that comes in some members, and then spreads from one member to another;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 and I saw what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	 I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	 and later on, I saw it rise like a worm at the shoulder, much faster than anything else, like a sharp knife when cutting from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	 the pain left that place and dug into the shoulder, and then a little later it ran through the whole body, until it came to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 Then I told him it was turning again around the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly surprised how it moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this kind of disease in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	 Furthermore, I wanted many that they had moved pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw it in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	 and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins exposed, and because of this appeared that constricted breath.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 And it did not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	 And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if she opens as we have said, lay her down quickly and then press on it until that constricted breath leaves that place.
et cauterize le leu;	 And cauterize the joint.
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 and if you do not see it in your eyes, then treat the one who protrudes the windbags (hernias), as with fetid pills or serapion pills, and similar things.
des saiettes	 Arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows or needles come in different types, depending on their shapes and the parts of the body they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	 The differences among them are that some have large points, small ones, thick ones, and sealed (closed).
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	 and those who have two angles, those who have tongues, and those which have pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	 and the one which falls in any member falls according to two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 or in the principal member (the brain), like the head, heart, liver, spleen, stomach, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	 When it falls [the shoulder] into any place of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you afterwards will appear to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	 Then it is necessary for you to remove this arrow, as death comes after in many ways.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 and if this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not fully in, pull it out, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	 And the sign of the brain when the arrow pierces the bone and there is a discharge from above the brain, is when scotomia and soreness and swelling and redness occur in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	 And sometimes without force from the nostrils, or ears.
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	 And sometimes the speech and voice are lost.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	 And jumps from the wound white matter resembling cheese, and also as if it were bursting with boiling water.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And if this sign appears, you should refrain from treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	 The sign of the arrow when it falls or pierces the heart is that it is near the left breast, and also as if it were embedded in a hard thing, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	 And sometimes the arrow becomes silent like cheese, and there is black blood in the wound, followed by coldness, cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 Therefore, the patient knows for certain that death is coming.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of an arrow that pierces the body is when a scab does not rise from the wound and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, breathes heavily and seeks warm air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	 And if an arrow falls in the bed of the sick, it should be extracted along the sides (of the body).
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	 and produces a great discharge, a great pain, and heavy breathing.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	 And all the limbs of the shoulders are moving.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead or stomach falls out by chance, anything from the undigested flesh may jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	If the arrowhead or abdomen falls out and something from the intestinal tract jumps out, there is no hope in the treatment nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	 If an arrow falls into the bladder, and it jumps out and comes out, and the patient feels great pain.
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	 The patient knows that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the hand, arm, neck, shoulder, backbone, waist, hips, legs, and those similar, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, for this reason you should do something else.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	 In a house, an arrow or spear fell into the root of the nose.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 I pulled it out from the other side beneath the fat of the ear and he was healed without injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	 And draw out an arrow that falls into the oil fat beneath the paper, and the arrow is stuck, and cannot be reached except the tip towards the skin, and the arrow was large as a Turkish bow, to the light touch, it touched the ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And the game was safe, and no bad accidents happened.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	 And draw out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow had Arabic ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 I was the bearded ones, and I became subtle until I drew it out, and the Christian was safe.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	 And draw out an arrow from the man who was wounded or in the belly, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	 And when he has passed XXX days, his dislocation does not change its position;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 I cut above the arrowhead, trapped it, and pulled it through without any mishap.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	 And if you wish to treat a man who has an arrow lodged in his back or a wound closed over it;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 and the arrow remains inside him, and does not disturb his natural positions or cause any harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	 And you wish to treat another man who has an arrow lodged in his face, and the wound is closed over it;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	 and it remains in this way suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	 and many similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	 And pull an arrow from the man of the kings who had fallen among the snow, and was slightly sloping to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	 And the arrow was completely withdrawn.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 I was summoned to treat her after she had fallen for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	 I felt her entire body with a delicate probe and did not feel anything.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 He feels sharp pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	 I thought it was an arrow tip. I applied a poultice with attracting and digestive properties because the wound did not inflame.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 And the arrow point appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	 I applied the poultice for several days, and healed the wound immediately, but the patient remained ill for a long time, feeling the arrow within his intestines.
et il le me dist.	 And he told it to him.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	 I apply the wound medicine that is corrosive to the arrowhead for many days until it opens, and then I test it, and feel the head of the arrow adhering to the place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	 Then, I align in the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow appears visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	 And it passed the limits beyond four months, and then I cut open the wound that I had sewn with the pincers, and pulled it apart from both sides, and could not pull it out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.
