Then, I did not cease to refine and devise means of tools, until I took the pincers well made, as described at the end of this chapter, when I pulled it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	 And the mirror judges that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 I will then restore it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	 I have told you the quality of the extraction of certain arrows, but place your care on this that I am not saying everything, for the books cannot cover all.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 but the wise masters compare themselves on very little things, and on what is present and failing, they discover nine works, and nine tools, for the explanation of foreign things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	 I say that arrows do not come out of the members where they are fixed except according to two ways.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	 By the joint where they enter, or from another side.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 and that which exits from there is an arrow passing through the flesh, and jumps out at times now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	 And if it does not jump out now, leave it until the flesh is healed around it, and let the exit be clean.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	 And if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it thus for several days and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 Then it jumps, and if it does not jump, pierce around with all the fine iron until the bones are loosened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	 If the arrow is stuck in the skull bone and goes to one of the brain ventricles, and any of the accidents I have mentioned occur to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 do not pull it out immediately, but leave it even for several days, because if the arrow reaches the sinuses, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrowhead is not embedded beyond the bone but has not been extracted, and the patient suffers for some days with bad condition, try to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	 If it is very stuck and cannot come out by force, administer remedies around it as I told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Cure the joint while it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	 And if the arrow has been placed within the body and cannot be seen, press as hard as you can.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	 And if you feel it, pull it out with any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	 And if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow because there is no bone, nerve or vein in the way, make an incision as wide as possible.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	 And pull the arrow out if you can, and if there are ears attached to it like a fish's spine, cut away the flesh that is stuck in by two parts as much as you can, then break or fold the ears of the arrow so you can pull it.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 Carefully make sure not to break the arrow, rather pull it out more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, pull down the leg to the joints, then draw, for extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	 If bleeding from the wound opposes you, introduce what we have said in its chapter for the cure.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	 And protect yourself from cutting the nerve and vein, and use an instrument as you can safely pull out the arrow, whether quickly or slowly, firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 Place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest aid that there can be; and if you cannot, place it as the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	 The arrow coming from another direction pierces something of it, or the skin is swollen near where we can see or feel it.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	 Cut then above, as long as the pliers can grasp it, and then pull it out.
si saut fuer maintenant.	 If it falls out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it [the dislocation] is held within the bone, you should turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	 And if it cannot fall out, leave it for a while and then continue the extraction until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	 If it is from the arrow shaft, push it all the way in.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	 If it falls out and you wish to give medicine, if there is a wound, administer the instrument, so that the tip of the arrow enters into the hair of the wound.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 Then push it again, and if the arrow is covered with hair, push the instrument to its tip entering in, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 If the arrowhead is touching [the body], it is necessary to cut around the affected area where the poison is, if possible, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	 If the arrow falls out of the head or side or abdomen or bladder or chest, and it is near, and you can cover it over, do so.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	 And guard against cutting the vein and the nerve, then pull it out, then make the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tweezers used to remove arrows is similar to an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	 And there are many ways to do it:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	 Large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The form of the buttock hair is similar to the feathers of a bird, for pushing the point of an arrowhead, as shown here: [no further English text provided]
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tweezers for pushing and extracting is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Incisions of the common body cavities
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	 Of the veins that heal are thirty-one, thus it has a head sixteen, which means:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	 The beating which are after the ears, which are called the twins "herbech";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	 and the two arteries that are in the two temples visible;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	 and the veins that are in the two eyes of the ears, which are called "aspirers";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	 and the vein that is under the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	 and the vein that is at the neck of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	 and the two tendons which are on the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	 and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins which are called "augheiriches";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	 The veins which are commonly called five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	 One is the cephalic, located on the left side of the ribcage, and common people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	 The middle one is called "fast", and it is made up of the cephalic and the basilic, and common people call it "vein of the heart".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 And the basilic is located on the right side of the ribcage, and common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the liver, and it is the one from which blood is let, which clearly opens up near the elbow.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	 And the savatalle is the vein that is between the ulnar and the annular, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	 And in the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	 One is under the ribcage on the left side, and the second is the shoulder blade which is at the wrist of the right side.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	 and the vein called "nasal," which is in the wrist of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And in the other leg are three veins beneath them.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	 The blood of the veins that are after the ears helps with ancient catarrhs and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	 and the qualities of the bloodsayer, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient and wipe the area or veins with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	 then tighten the patient's neck with a noose until two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head;
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	 When the finger joint hurts beneath your thumb, press on it firmly.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	 Then take the lance, and push it under the vein up to the bone, then pull your hand all along the vein above, and strike and the skin and vein well two strokes through it, and make blood come out as much as you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 then hold it tightly until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 and I have already said the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	 The healing of the two arteries that are in the temples, is good for migraines, headaches, and eye diseases, and for corneas with dry eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	 And the qualities of the healer are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	 and it is that the patient stretches his neck, until both veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	 and feel the pulse at the base of your throat, then press firmly.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	 then cut the vein above your throat index, and insert the needle beneath it, and draw up the vein, and seal it, as you have done in the other two veins, and stop the bleeding according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	 then release the patient, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 and then fold it and let it heal until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 and we have spoken about its sealing and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	 The sanitation of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the sanitation of the skull for the diseases of the face old and new, and migration, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	 And the quality is that the patient turns their neck while twisting it, until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 Then take the instrument called "fosseur", which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	 And place the point on the vein, and press down with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 Then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein when it is healthy and never use fire more than once.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	 Moreover, the flames should not be too sharp;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	 And the bone is broken obliquely, because it is close, and by chance, the flame breaks when it is fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	 The sawn of the two veins that are in the eyelids helps the eyes, and at the tear-duct, and at the conjunctiva, and at the oil duct in the eye, and at facial diseases;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	 And the quality of their saw is that the patient stretches his neck by twisting some cord, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 Then the saw, and it should be the sawed bone, a little long and wide, for there is no cartilage.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	 And if the flame is fine, by chance it may break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	 Then make a dressing of blood, as much as you need, and then sew it up with cloth, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	 The cleansing of the vein from the nose is effective against headache, smallpox, and diseases of the face, such as migraines and redness that appear in the face, and especially when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	 And the qualities of cleansing are that the patient should tighten their neck, then hold their nose with your left hand and take subtle flame long, and push it into the space between the two nostrils because the vein does not open well, and the pus will start to flow out.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	 and do not go too deep and let the blood flow according to your need, then leave it for a night because it recovers quickly.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 And this is the form of fire:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	 The salve of the two guindges helps in the straightening of the ankle, and at the beginning of the fracture, and in mixing wounds, and in many diseases, and in stopping inflammation, and in corroding, and in herpes, and stomach ulcers;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	 and the quality of the salve is such that the patient stretches his neck under one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	 and the master being above the patient's head, and the patient lying on the seat, then open the vein long enough a little widely, then draw out the blood moderately, or as much as necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	 then tie up another vein, then untie the ligature, and hold the veins moderately so that the patient does not strangle;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 And let it (the wound) remain until morning, so that it heals.
de la sainie des leivres	 Of the livestock health
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The treatment of mouth boils also helps with cold in the mouth and corruption of the gums, and cuts and sores around the mouth.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	 Then the quality of healing is to make the patient sit before you and hold their neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	 Then turn the jaw, and look at the two holes, one is at the right jaw and the other at the left, and they can be recognized by being black, and by the small black veins surrounding them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 Hold one and the other, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, hold the larger one of each pair, and the same applies to the two holes above and below, for it is done in the same way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 Of the livestock health below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	 The punctures below the tongue help after the puncture of the head and are for the stretching of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	 And the qualities of puncturing are that the patient should sit between the sun and open his mouth, and look down on each side for a black hole.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 Keep both [shoulders] healthy then, and do not go too deep [into them], because underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	 The veins in question are commonly healed in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	 Or when pricking everywhere with burning myrtle large, or olive oil subtle as you can pierce through, and is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 and are wide and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very renowned, and it is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	 And it is necessary to open swollen veins full of thick blood, and containing large and turbulent blood.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 and this is the shape of olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more pointedly subtle, and is for healing subtle veins where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	 The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are beneath the throat, and neck, and stomach.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 And the lord must drain it in a clear way, and empty the artery that is below it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	 And if it touches the artery, and bleeding comes out, you should compress it, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And it must not be pressing the flame, but cutting it like a pincer.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	 If the bladder does not open manifestly, you should incise it and change another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	 Or you wish to drain anything from it, or you open the vein in its place on the arm.
elle apert manifestement;	 It opens manifestly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And press the flame with pincers, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	 If you wish to locate the place of bleeding, then you must also incise the arm, so that you touch the vein as much as you know the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	 Then sign the joint with a hot iron, then bind the arm, and press the vein with fire.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	 Also ensure that you do not injure the artery when you see the joint swell, as it is an artery:
eschui la donques.	 cut it off then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	 If you see it protrude upwards like a child's urine and the limb is red and thin, know that it is not an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	 Therefore hasten then, put your thumb on top for a long time, then cut off your thumb where it becomes pale, as this often happens:
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	 bind the arm and leave it alone, let the patient not move it:
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and be careful, let it not move until it is drained.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	 And if the artery is not stopped and it escapes, and the medicine is not present with you, then cut the artery open, for its head will recede.
et estainche li sans.	 If the blood does not flow (back) from the wound, and it bleeds, then stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	 Take a strip of willow bark, cut it and take one half and bind it on top until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	 If the blood does not flow (back) from the wound, that is good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	 If it does bleed, heal it as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 And the stopping of bleeding should not be excessive in various positions due to the small size of the wound and the thickness of the bandage on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	 The vein in the middle helps to drain blood from the head above and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and the cephalic, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	 and it is necessary for the surgeon to pierce along the nerve that is below, and if it pricks too deep, and he discovers the nerve, and it swells and the patient becomes sickly, and in case it does not heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	 and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any man due to his subtlety, then you must anesthetize the patient with the instrument.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 cut the nerve as far as your power allows.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	If there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	 The vein of the cephalic helps, which draws blood from the head and assists the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 And it is necessary to cauterize by pricking with olive oil or myrtle fire, for it is the safest of all veins, because there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	 Furthermore, seek the easiest joint, and do not hurt anything the first time, and repeat if necessary.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 And by chance, the joints swell in some men, where you should seek first, but do not hurt anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of urine is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	 The first thing you need to know about cautery is that it should not be done except for maintaining health and avoiding future diseases.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	 And the cauterization should be performed in one of the three veins that are called:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	 This means "It is to know, cephalic, fasting, and basilic.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	 And it should be bled at the beginning of the springtime, during Lent and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 And it should be bled every other day, after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	 The bleeding administered for diseases has no set time, but whenever need arises, day or night, in all hours and at any time.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 And it is not necessary to bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor women in childbirth for the first four months up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Old people over sixty years old should not be treated.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	 And whenever anyone wants to be bled, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary that they empty the intestines with a light enema if they have retained much filth, so that the veins do not release superfluous waste into the main organs.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	 A person who is overly salted with foods or drunk, so much that he becomes intoxicated, or urinating excessively, should not be cured.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	 If someone is sick after suffering from colic, vomiting, stomach upset, multiple intercourse with women, heavy labor, staying awake and fasting, or anything related to the body or weapon, they should not be treated.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	 Then refine the humors if the patient is obese from foods and drinks and medications, if you have that power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	 Then immerse or bathe him if nothing prevents it, to refine the blood, and heal the wound around the third part of the vein as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	 And keep oneself from work, and from pain, and from lust, and from similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	 And bind it and tighten, and let the laceration be higher than the one being healed, and rub the arm two or three times, then gently pull out the thread above halfway, for if it is too tight or loose, the wound will not heal correctly.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	 And then rub the wound with your hands until the veins swell, and feel for them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 Then moisten the bandage with a little bit of old oil, then place your thumb of your left hand on that vein under the wound where you want to lance it, so that the vein does not break or tear when lancing.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	 For there are veins that run like cords in the body, and some of these have become filled with pus, so that when you place fire upon them, they shrink away from the flame and cannot open the vein, and such is one of those.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 If the vein opens, the wound becomes too narrow, which is why the one who draws the cord must be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	 But if the vein opens for the first time, that is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	 If not, start again a little below that place or immediately above it, if the joint is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	 And if the joint is swollen and the patient is afraid, let it rest for a day or two and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	 Perhaps abscess pusules will come.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	 Do not immerse or bathe, then clean the wound if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	 And if the wound is small or shallow and you doubt that it will not bleed much as you see, trust in that very wound itself completely with direct fire.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	 Open a little quickly, but only when the joint is swollen;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 For this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	 If you see the wound swelling, do not start draining pus, but put a little oil of linen on it, for it cools the body from the blood, and the linseed oil heals in this place where the oil is applied.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	 and administer the linen oil to each wound that you drain pus, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	 and this same thing is made of three parts and a bowl from them when it is applied to the wound.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 if the pus is too thick, strain it when it becomes too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	 If a large abscess comes, which often happens when the wound is not drained until this time or when the opening of the vein is small, then hurry, and put on the wound a wet sponge with hot vinegar and oil, and hold it for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	 And it is necessary that you make this after the blood flow from the vein, and if it remains in its place for some days without any blackness or greenness, it does not harm.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if you see, place something of aloes or myrrh beneath it in the cavity, poultice, or similar thing.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	 And many times abscess and appearance at the opening of the basilica occur.
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	 Place your hand on it then, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, this is a bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	 Therefore, do not place anything from what we have said, because by chance it may touch the artery without.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 But make a dry plaster to harden the place, then cure it with other remedies until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw out blood from each person according to the quantity of its strength and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	 If the wound is black, let it drain until it turns red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	 and if you see a swelling, let it become thin;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	 and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	 For the person who is full and open, and needs bloodletting, make a larger wound, and let the veins be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	 And for the weak one, do the opposite, and it must be drained little by little and often, and it must be drained by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And this method of drainage is safe from contamination of blood and compression of nerves, and it is more effective than long draining rather than wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	 And to the one whose body needs draining, it is necessary to give soft bread soaked in grape juice beneath.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 If he is burned, let him be bled three or four times; and if he has a cold complexion, let him fast before the draining, with soft bread soaked in sweet syrup or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicory, and a fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if the wound is bleeding profusely after dislocation, it is necessary that you apply a paste of charcoal and sweet-smelling subtle syrup, and use other things as we have said in the section or chapter on fainting, for blood evacuation.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If you want to dislocate someone's arm and then relocate it at another time, when it has been weakened by much bleeding, it should be done little by little, according to the amount of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to dislocate someone's arm after the first bleeding, and has a strong heart, should wait 9 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to be bled from another part, should be bled on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	 There is much blood within the body which has become heated, causing fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	 It is necessary to draw out a large amount and widen the opening until it can pass through a funnel;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	 then you should follow all the conditions of health, and place your hand on top of the feet when it is healthy, so that death does not come in its place, and this happens often when the healers are negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	 and it is not necessary to dislocate the arm and draw blood again if the opening is closed, but you should press firmly.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	 If it is bent, extend the arm as far as possible, for that would be wrong;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	 but let it remain healthy a second time.
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 If you burn at the tip of the flame until the vein which is frozen opens up, and place the piece of linen soaked in vinegar on it and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if a vein has burst, let it be and do not compress it until the abscess is pacified.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If it requires drawing blood a second time, draw it from the same place, or another vein, or the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is safer to use instead of the one in the neck because it is composed of different vessels.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	 And the way to heal is that the patient plunges their hand into hot water until the flesh becomes red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	 Then bind it gently, so that the vein is visible, then pierce it carefully with a small needle, not wide or long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	 and make the incisions wide, and prick the joint of the hand carefully, and if it does not bleed, then immerse the hand in hot water, and let the blood come out into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	 if it is cold, do not immerse the hand in hot water, because it makes it colder rather than warmer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 and the pricking of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there are neither arteries nor nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	 The pricking of the thumb of the right hand is useful for all liver diseases, and this is how it works:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	 Hold the hand, and push it into hot water, until the vein has been opened, if you can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	 and if the artery is cut through entirely, and you cover it all over, it will not hurt at all.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 and do not go too deep, because the nerves are bare beneath all the skin there; then replace the hand in hot water, so that the wound does not freeze, and it cannot heal.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let the blood as much as needed, put oil and linen over the wound to heal quickly, and do this for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The purification of the hand on the left side is beneficial for the disease of paralysis, and it should be done in the same way as I told you concerning the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The incision of the saphenous vein is beneficial for all the diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of phlegm, and disease of the kidneys, and the thighs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	 And the quality of its artery is such that the patient must press his foot in hot water and rub on the vein until it ruptures, and tie it above the joint of the foot.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	 And if the vein is at the ankle, then you must go upwards along the leg a great deal.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 Treat the wound with a larger reed or at the ankle, if necessary.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	 If you treat it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are beneath, and treat it through as when sewing;
et soit li flaimes anesil.	 And let the flames be quenched.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the leg cannot be extracted, place it in the water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	 If the wound requires sainying for the first time, then start the second one a little above, because the flesh is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the tendon of the other limb equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The salted area of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the foot, and its blister is worth the pain of the heel when it is hot with blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	 And the quality of his healing is that the patient immerses himself in water or a bath and strains above the ankle for four fingers while turning, because otherwise the vein will not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	 And if it opens, let him heal in all possible ways and by crossing over (it).
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 It is better to cover it, because the wound is exposed and very sensitive to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	 And if you do not treat it, no remedy for the wound will open or close at the back of the foot, and beware of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	 Make as much pressure on the blood as you can see, then undo the bandage, put cotton on it and tie it again.
ele est maintenant sanee.	 It is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 of blistering sores
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	 Blisters are made of horns, or hare's foot, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	 and blistering is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	 To draw and attract blood, or to not wound.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	 And this venetization (or cauterization) which is called "not wounding" follows two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	 or it is with all fire, or without fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	 And venetization (or cauterization) which is done by wounding and bloodletting is made in 14 parts of the body, so that the one who is all head is completely in the upper part (of the body).
et li autres est emmi le col;	 and the others are in the neck.
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	 and the others in the two sides of the neck.
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	 and the veins below the chin.
et li ventouse des II espaules;	 and the veins of both shoulders.
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	 and the veins above the ankles.
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	 and the veins in both arms.
et les ventouses des II jambes;	 and the veins in both legs.
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	 And the blisters of the two shins;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	 And the blisters do not bleed, unless of small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason should not be opened, if one does it as with the lancing of a vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor hot fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is evacuated.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	 And if by necessity of diseases it is necessary to blister, or for custom, then we will administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at each time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	 because there are some who, when they have to blister, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	 And for those who find swelling and redness in their body, in their face, neck, and darkness of the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	 And for those who find a spot of blood in their mouth, and the tongue has swollen, and they are spitting blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if there are those who faint, see blood in urine and nosebleed and other similar symptoms.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	When we see these signs and especially when it is in the month [of the disease], we order to bleed after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	 The pain of the mouth helps with the pain in the head ... which comes to the eyes, and it is not advisable that this be after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	 And this ventilation is in the place of mouth pain, and it should not be used by those who have a cold constitution or diarrhea, because it does them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 And therefore, it is not advisable for those who watch, or have a cold head disease, to use [the treatment].
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal themselves become obtuse, and for this reason, the blister should be placed a little lower due to the risk of becoming obtuse.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	 The ventosation (ventilation) is in the location of the sinuses in the skull and base, and for this reason it is beneficial for the narrowing of the nose passage, and for fracture of the nasal channel, and for swelling, and for congestion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 It should be pushed gently, because if it remains too tightly closed, it causes obstruction of the throat or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	 The ventosation in the ribs of the neck is good for headaches, otalgia (ear pain), migraines, strangulation, and tooth root pain, and it is in the location of the sinuses in the basilica.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 It is necessary that you command the lord to press his hand for insertion, not to hit the artery, and there should be no flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	 Ventilating beneath the chin is useful for mouth diseases and for corruption of gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	 and it is in the location of the sinuses of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilations of the shoulders are good for disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	 Ventilating the ribs is as much as three veins in the arm, because it attracts blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 Command the lord not to pierce too deeply, because the flesh is bare of skin, and it knows beneath black and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	 Ventilation above the rump is useful for hemorrhoids in the root and diseases beneath it, and the ventilator should be large and made of eagle feathers, as it needs to draw well.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	 And possibly, if it is delicate, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	 and causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	 The leg ulcers open widely because they draw blood from the whole body, and are like the old aches of the kidneys, and the bladder, and the scrotum; they destroy the flowers.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	 They are in the region of the hip bones and the wrists, and yet they weaken the body after long usage, and cause pus to appear in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	 The method of applying the ulcer is to first empty it, then moisten it promptly, and apply it quickly, moving it evenly, and not stopping until you see the region turn red and swell, and open the redness of the blood.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	 Then heat (or cauterize), and apply the cupping glasses, and take care in the arrangement of the body, for there are some who have tender flesh and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	 It is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and one deep puncture.
et suce legierement.	 Suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	 And if the flesh is thick, it is necessary to strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	 The first time is to make a passage for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	 And if the flesh is very thick, it is necessary to strike the third time:
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	 When we want to draw blood drop by drop, we should only prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	 And if we want a lot of blood, we reward it often:
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	 And if the bone is thin, it should be pierced entirely, and the wound should be closed so that the pores are perforated; for those with thick and hard skin and narrow pores, you must anoint the joints of the blisters with stimulating and dissolving oil.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	 If it is thin, use violet oil, sweet almond oil, or the oil of seed from cucumber.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if it is in a vein, use watercress oil, lily oil, chamomile oil or other similar oils.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluidity is large and cold, take amat oil, or balm of Gilead oil, or anise oil, and others like it.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the one whom you are treating has tender flesh and wide pores, no oil should be applied; instead, it should be washed after ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or water of morello cherries, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or some similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And one who has much moisture, if he rises from bed, should do so with asafetida or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	 And those with excess fluid should rise from old wine, or juice of blood, or the decoction of dill or chamomile, or other similar.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	 And it is not necessary to use a cupping glass before bathing or in bath, but after the bath for an hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And one must not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he warm himself, when he should be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	 Keep watch over the one who is being bled, for he is choleric, and if he lacks it, he becomes too sharp and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	 He should take cold things such as pomegranates, endive, lettuce and similar items.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And eat lean meat, veal from a castrated bull, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	 And the one who has a cold constitution should take honey syrup, sweet-smelling wine of moderate age, and eat coarse bread, lean meat and small birds and sparrows.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	 And on the day when he will turn himself, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	 It is necessary to give some men sometimes tricolor or musk to the wind, or after, for strengthening the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And let it be subtle, but one should not drink it if he is hot.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	 The wounds placed for cutting are those placed on the liver, spleen, gout, stomach and bowels, back and loins and haunches, since these limbs do not bear being cut upon or pierced except to draw blood from one member to another, as we do with the mammary glands when they swell;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	 to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we place wounds on the stomach and bowels to reduce the limb;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	 And alleviate the pain when there is an obstruction or arrow, if possible, draw out the obstruction by its attracting virtue, or dislodge the arrow from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	 Similarly, it is done when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, and these winds are treated empty because they are sucked dry only.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 And sometimes they are treated with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water, as in pleurisy diseases, and in this way the wind is filled with hot water or water in which healing herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the blister to be treated with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	 It should be two fingers wide and half a palm long, and it should pierce the middle of the wound near the muscle, as with an awl, and it should be made of linen, soft in front so that it does not irritate the patient when placed on the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	 And take in the middle of a plowshare or iron bar a yard's length for putting a candle-stand in position, and make them big or small according to the diseases and age of those who use it.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 For the swellings of children are different from those of the old, and those of the thin from those of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	 And this swelling should be placed thus on the member.
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	 Take the candle of wax or linen thread and place it in the swelling across the rod that is in the swelling so that the light is at the bottom of the swelling, so as not to burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	 Then place it on the member and your hands should be over the hole as we have said, so that when one looks, if there is steam, remove the swelling.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And wrap it with linen as before, and renew it often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	 In the cupping of illness caused by pleurisy in all its acuteness, it should not have a prick or puncture, and it is only applied when it is full of water. It is placed on the affected body part only for a short time.
et c’est li forme:	 and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	 Blisters are applied only to the parts where cupping cannot be used due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	 and in open areas of skin, such as fingers or toes, and similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	 The quality of the blister user is that when you find blisters in clear, sweet, and healthy-looking water, you should take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	 And place them in a soft warm bath until they are familiarized, and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	 Then let it be drained of blood and bled, then rub the limb until it is red, and apply leeches on it.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 And when they are full and warm, if there is a place where leeches can be applied, apply them, for it is very beneficial.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	 If not, lift the arm (or limb) high and then let it hang down, do this well, and then sprinkle it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	 And if the arms are too far from the body by the leeches, wet a linen cloth in cold water and put it on, until the leeches are dried.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	 And if there are no bones, place it on broken glass, or similar things, until it is boiled.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	 And you place half-peeled beans on it, and leave them until they adhere to the place, then it will be healed now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 and if you need more, take other soothing herbs.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	 And if the soothing herbs do not want to be taken, you rub the place with fresh blood, or stick a needle there until pus comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will adhere.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And when you see that they are weeping, sprinkle some powder of aloe and of crushed silk or ashes on it, then they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures (breaks)
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with setting fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	 Learn, dear child, that the foolish man should avoid this chapter, as he will never see any ancient books or read a letter from them.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	 and for this reason, the knowledge is foreign in our land, as I never found anyone good at it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	 and I know nothing about it, except by the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have practiced medicine based on them, and by experience, and by the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 and I have described for you in this chapter what is contained, summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are brought forth, as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we explain the summary of this book's content and the chapters where the wise put their understanding, and dwell on truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	 I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary for you to straighten the patient from one side and the other, unless anything prevents you, such as weakness of body, or infants, or old people;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	 or if the time is not very hot, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	 and do not eat cold food, meaning raw meats, or drink wine, or eat fatty foods, and do not fill oneself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of abscess heat, or expansion of matter in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 if the patient returns to his former government as he used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that the patient be fed on foods that cause thick stools, or have viscosity like cooked barley in water and peas, and beef, and pork, and veal, and mutton, and eggs, and fresh fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this thick stool, the healing of the fracture is quicker.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	 And know that the broken bones of old people and weak ones cannot be well regained nor sutured according to their nature due to the looseness of limbs, not those who are too tender as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	 but it has no cure, reset above the broken bone and hold the member together firmly, until it heals as it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 and do not let him work at all, and therefore nourish him with thick meats as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head (skull) is different from that of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all ways of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture which goes towards the elbow, and another in sharpening, like the tip of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	 And in each way he should have his device, and his equipment proper for the restoration according to what memory comes to him.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	 And the fracture of the bone is recognized by this that the joint is twisted and opened widely, and sounded with the probe, and pressed with the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	 And when there is no twisting or damage [to the joint], and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no breakage.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 but it may have twisting, crack, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	Do not move the hand at all, but place medicine on it that comes afterwards, and then hold it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	 And know that the breaks that are in the joint, and the two parts separated, you must now put them equally together, so that abscesses heal quickly.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	 and if an abscess heals quickly, let it be left for as many days as the abscess is subsided.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	 then put it equally in the muscle that you can easily and skillfully move, and know that the restoration of this is easier than the restoration where there are fractures.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 Then hold, as required hereafter.
