Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	 If the bone is broken into pieces, let it be set with two parts, whether it is hand or foot, or at your hand if it is one of the smaller members, or with two cords, or with one cord and at your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	 And set the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the member are disjoined, if you can, reset all the additions in their places with every means possible, and make sure through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And adjust well the two joints of the bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	 Feel it with your hand if it seems not to be quite right.
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	 Straighten it well, but do not strain it too much, nor press it as those who make it swell and contract the member through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	 And when the member is set straight, restrain the patient from moving it, not paying attention to him neither sleeping nor waking, not turning or in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And keep the limbs so secure that they feel no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	 For when it feels no pain, it is not in place, and you must put it in such a position that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	 And ensure that it is placed correctly, so that it does not become twisted when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 The qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members are diverse in smallness and largeness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	 For there are small members such as fingers, thumbs, and others.
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	 You must wrap soft and thin linen cloth around it.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	 For those that are large, such as the thighs and legs.
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	 It is necessary to wrap with a wide and hard bandage, for the wide bands embrace the entire large limb, and they hold it equally from all sides so that there is no leak.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	 Then wrap light bandages around it, three or four times according to the limb, and hold your hand slightly on the entire bandage, then go above the break and hold less, so that the break is held but slightly less, then move the break away a little.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	 soften the bandage gradually, as you take a large part of the healthy flesh, then take another bandage, and wind again directly over the broken place.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	 then return to the part below the break, and hold it moderately, not too strongly nor too loosely, as we said in the first lesson above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 Then put between the joints soft linen or cloth strips that are all even, then tie it all together with a bandage, and then place well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	 If there is swelling or an abscess, put on top soothing substances for the abscess and one that reduces swelling, and leave it like that for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 Then tighten the splints, and they should be half the width of a thick cane or pole used for splitting wood, or reeds of palm, and according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	 but it is necessary that the splint placed on the break should be a little larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	 And let it be as long as is necessary for the limb, whether small or large.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	 then pull upwards on the stitches as you did at the first joint, then tie it with thread coming from above, as in the first joint when breaking.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	 The gap is too narrow now, make it wider.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	 It must be that the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, and it should be of flax thread.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish people who make their knots with twisted flax threads, and that is a great error, because the knot will not be even if it is too thin, and it should not have less than two fingers' space between each stitch.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is pierced by the limbs of the ribs after setting them in healthy bones, place linen or flax padding beneath them to prevent swelling.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is broken and the nerves are torn, I will tell the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to hold bones of broken members all day long on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	 For when the limbs are large, no needles should be inserted before five or seven days, or more, according to your certainty of the abscess healing.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	 And here is the method for ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation and twisting:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 And it is that you take flour that is kept near the mill walls, and mix with enough egg, and put this mixture, neither too clear nor too thick, and apply it, and this is the common method for plaster restoring fractures in various ways, and equally for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	 Another method for plaster restoring the fracture, dislocation and twisting:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	 Take [the following]: abrasive and lardanium and vinegar and asafetida and Arabic gum and myrrh; mix them, according to recipe X.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	 Myrrh and aloes, according to recipe V.
alechil VIIII З.;	 alum VIII, [according to] recipe IX.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	 and make it into powder, and mix it with egg yolk.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	 If the constitution of the man is hot, use this plaster because it has good composition and quickly restores broken bones and benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	 Another way to make a plaster that helps with twisting pains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	 take myrrh and lardanium, according to recipe X.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	 Myrrh and aloes, according to recipe IX.
acaice VI З.;	 The dislocation arises from any displacement of its place; therefore, it cannot move, and the limb is malformed. (This sentence seems to be a continuation of the previous one)
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Pound well, and crush and mix with vinegar or abundant egg, and administer it. (This sentence seems to be giving instructions for treating a dislocation)
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	 Another way to treat a dislocation and swollen joints, and to relieve the pain that occurs, is to cut the bone with a tool, and break it. (This sentence seems to be giving additional instructions for treating a dislocation)
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Take new linen, wet it in vinegar and cooked oil, and place it on the joint. (This sentence seems to be giving further instructions for treating a dislocation)
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This plaster does not heal, but it is good for alleviating abscess pain and bone fracture pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	 Another way to treat dislocated bones is: (This sentence seems to be introducing another treatment method for dislocations)
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	 Take dried fig leaves, and leaves of common pauper's knotweed (also known as common nettle), grind them together to make a paste.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another method of plaster for the healing of the broken bone and for promoting the healing of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	 Take the root of mallow, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of wheat, each in equal parts;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 and grind, and boil together with wine, and if the limbs are scalded, boil it with moist coriander water or broth, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of amputation stronger than the first, when an abscess hard comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	 Take equal parts of the roots of mallow, flax seeds, wild sage, horehound, and meadowsweet, as well as flowers of violets and chamomile;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 grind them together, boil in salt water or sweet water or wine, depending on the heat of the limb and its rest period.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that no other substance besides a mixture of beeswax and oil should be applied to a broken limb for restoration, and it should neither be too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen states that for restoring a broken limb, one should apply warm dry substances such as myrrh, aloes, incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	 Another way of applying the plaster is useful for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	 Take a handful of crushed human copes or goose feathers, and equal amounts of resin and wax, and grind them together to make the plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	 And then remove a small amount after that, ensuring the patient does not feel any pain and that the bones have not moved from their place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	 If you do not remove it for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	 And if pain or itching occurs at the place, without rest, swelling or inflammation, hurry and remove it immediately; leave the plaster off.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	 and take a light cloth, sea sponge dampened with water, dip it in water, lift the place, until the itching stops and the pain is relieved.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	 Leave the member to rest for an hour, then put dry linen on it, dampen it with vinegar or rose oil, and tie it up tightly until you are certain the abscess has been heated.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	 Remove the inflammation from the member and alleviate the pain, then begin wrapping again subtly, a little plaster, and do not strain it too much as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the abscess has burst, become red, painful and swollen, and if you need plaster and linen, then suture it as you did before evenly.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	 And if no improvement occurs in the member as we have said, do not remove the wrapping for more than 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	 And never leave it for 20 days, as we see, until the fracture heals and the wound approaches the skin.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	 Then hold it more firmly than before, and swell the flesh, as I have said earlier.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	 If you see the joint become dry beyond what is necessary, know that nutrients cannot reach it.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	 Therefore, immerse the joint in warm water every time you dislocate it, and do this three times a day, and slightly loosen the bandage.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	 By this work, then cut off the nutrients from the limb and heal quickly what the foolish doctor leaves twisted.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 This is harmful, and it is a work full of fear, and I see nothing but laziness and working incorrectly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	diverse methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	 There are many ways to break bones, and various shapes, and the reasons for them are different;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	 For there are fractures that are made by sword blow, and the hilt strikes the whole bone up to the shaft which is beneath the bone, just like a wedge or a ram.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 And this kind of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	 When the sword strikes the bone from above and pierces through it, this kind of fracture is called "absolue".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	 And the wounds caused by these two types of fractures can be either large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a bruise filled with blood, or a wound or arrow wounds, or falling upon a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If it is a swelling that approaches the membrane underneath the bone, or it is on the bone and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	 And if the wound is repaired in the bone as thin as a horse's hair and the crack is small, then this kind of fracture is called "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	 And if the wound is made by striking a stone or falling or something similar, and it drives the bone fragment downwards, and the ends of the bones are even like smiths when they make pots over fire.
si entre li piere dedens.	 If the arrow enters within (the body).
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	 And this happens more often with those who have wet or soft bones, such as in children;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	 and it occurs in all these ways of fracture where small fragments are separated, as is the case with shattered bones;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And I will speak about its place (the bone).
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all manners of breaks by the drawing on them, and the testing inquiry, and through the corruption of flesh that is above. (line-by-line translation)
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The resemblance of the capillary is known by those who, when the bone is exposed and scraped above, if the break appears black. (line-by-line translation)
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a break, take care of the patient's circumstances, and if you see any bad accident, as vomiting of blood, loss of consciousness, stretching, swelling, fever, the hairs coming out and reddening, and other symptoms in various dispositions, it cannot heal with doubt. (line-by-line translation)
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an overwhelming accident, and you hope for salvation, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the splinter first comes to you in winter, it must be removed before the fourteenth day at the bone's mouth.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone does not rot, and the accidents we have mentioned come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	 And if the fracture of the bone comes up to the membrane that covers the brain, you must cut the divided part as follows:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	 And it is that you grab the patient's head, and expose the bone in all ways that you can, and above the wound as much as you can, and if blood comes out to expose the bone or an abscess boils up, help with whatever is needed, and it is that you fill the place with dampened linen soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	 and make the wound rest until the abscess boils are calmed down, and be sure of the flow of blood.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	 then start around the bone to cut, and this is done in two ways of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 One method is that you make a narrow cut in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then insert another, larger incision.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	 And the second method is that you have a variety of sizes, some narrow and others wide, pointed, and made of iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	 and work lightly, lest you pierce the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	 If the bone is protruding and hard, it is necessary that you pierce around it, in such a way that you provide sizes with tapers, but not so deep as to go beyond the bone of the skull, and above the point there should be a margin or circle that does not let the point go beyond the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	 and you must have more of them, so that each one comes in its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have tapers for all cases.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	 And this is the form of the three ways of lancing:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	 The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place the lancet on the bone and turn it with your fingers until you feel that the bone has been punctured.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	 Then move the lancet to another spot a little after, and do this all around, then cut the space of the bone that is between the fractures, and do this more subtly than you can and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone into your hand, or any of the instruments that you have like pliers or tweezers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	 And be careful not to touch the brain nor the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	 When you have punctured and treated the bone, it is necessary that you reset the sharpness of the bone to any other instrument resembling an incisor, but it must be thinner and more subtle than the other incisors.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	 And if there remain any small bones, no scales, lightly separate them with the instruments.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 then heal the wound of tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	 And the other way of work is that which Galen said, which is more secure.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	 and he greatly commands it, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture moves open; so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place it under the head of this concave incisor, as shown in the following figure:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	 And do not cut from one side, but the parts should be equally on two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	 then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly break the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth that is beneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 if it is hard against the bone, break the bone lightly, for one breaks it too much and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate through to the membrane, and the bone is only split from above, and there are small fragments, then after smoothing it, remove the scales with a sharp rasp, having different amounts as necessary, in order to provide the most suitable amount for each place, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Start with a large rasp, then proceed with finer ones, and do not stop until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	 In each of the other hairy growths or subtle fractures, you should apply a remedy according to its nature.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	 and this is something not easily answered by one who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	 And if the wound is exposed, you should take linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	 then take another linen cloth doubled over two or three times, moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	 and do this more gently than you can, so as not to burden the wound, then administer another thread on top, but do not tighten it any more than necessary to cover the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	 And let it remain for a day or two, until the abscess subsides, then release it, and administer medicines as with lilies, flour of wheat, incense powder, Aristolochia, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	 And from these things make powder, and apply it to the wound, and administer immediately medicines without harm or bitterness.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	 And watch that the wound is always clean, do not leave any ointment or clotted blood on it, for when clotted blood accumulates on the brain-cloth, it will rot and corrupt, causing great harm to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 For if anything bitter is applied to it, it will rot from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Then take care, if any harmful event befalls the patient as we have said, it is full of doubtful meaning.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	 And if blackness does not come violently except for the medicine that has been put on it, which possesses such power, then you should take a part of honey, and 3 parts of rose oil, and mix them with linen cloth, and apply it on the affected area.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then you should treat it according to the methods of treatments that are necessary, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	 Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above can be broken, or one by itself, because they are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	 and the one beneath is cartilage, and does not break, unless it causes a blow or twisting, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	 And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should place your little finger or thumb into the nose, and align the break within your index finger's tip, and at the back of the nose, until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And do this gently, so the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part near the neck and the thumb cannot reach its place, you must align it with the head of a ruler, a little bigger.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	 If the fracture is in two parts, then fix it in the same manner, and hasten to restore it on the first day if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has subsided, then bind the end of the wound with linen cloths if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	 Or you bind the other side if there is a fracture there.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	 And let the bandages be as thick as they fill the openings of the wound.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And they said any remedy that one must moisten tents with butter, and churn every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	 It does not seem good to me, but it is necessary that they be moistened with egg white and flour powder mixture.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 Then let the tendon remain tense, until the bone hardens, and the cartilages become hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	 And sometimes feathers of goose are used instead of tendons, and if it is soaked in wool, held with a bandage, and the break is kept, then blow on the wound while the patient breathes.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	 or do what you think is best.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the new (opening) while you are working on it, put either beeswax or cotton wool soaked in rose oil, or a small piece of lignum aloes, there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	 And if an abscess does not come, apply plaster on the outside with flour from wheat and powder of incense, mixed with egg yolk, then place light compresses on top but do not bind the feathers.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	 and if the break of the feathers is small, and it breaks into small pieces, take them with suitable instruments, then stitch the wound, and treat it with things that are appropriate for the purpose, such as plasters and ointments.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if there is no wound within nor in the nose, treat it with tents, and place plasters of wool until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured below and there is no wound outside, and the break is only displaced and not broken through to the inside, but rather bent within, this can be recognized easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	 If the fracture is in the right side, you must insert your index finger into the patient's mouth:
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	 And if the fracture is in the left jaw bone, insert your right index finger and gently push the fracture inside, adjust it to the other side with the left hand and hold it steady:
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is dislocated in two places, then you must administer extension of two parts, equal in size.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	 If the teeth move or are broken, hold them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then place a collar on the fractured jaw bone and put a double cloth on it:
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	 Place a wide and long bandage or piece of leather on the jawbone, securing it above the muscles that you can reach, and tell the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	 And if you see the figure changes, dislocate it on the third day, then reset it to its original position.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	 and place a plaster on top of it, with powder from the mill along with egg or flour of sesame, after you have removed the sore.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	 and place a thin linen plaster on top of it, and if the plaster adheres to it, and the position of the patient does not change, leave it until it heals.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	 it often heals within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, bring what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	 and if there is a fracture and wound together, be careful not to remove any piece of the bone;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	 use subtle tools for removing the straws suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, you should widen it with fire as necessary.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and none remain, close the wound if it is wide, and put on one dressing suitable for that purpose, to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	From the lock (or fastening)
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	 The forceps break multiple times before, towards the shoulder, and these fractures are in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	 or it is broken and dislocated in two places, and it is in several fragments, and is the easiest to restore.
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	 or there is a fracture with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	 And the work [procedure] is when there is a fracture with an open wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder which feels the forceps are broken.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	 and the other extends the neck towards the affected area.
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	 then make the fracture equal to your hands, so that the shape is as required, and there should be no protrusion or appearance of deformity.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	 And if you need to extend more, place a round ball of fabric or linen on the patient's shoulder, and it should be as large as necessary for your needs.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And you shall stretch and lift the limb, and hold the shoulder with your hand, so that you align the fracture as necessary.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder out of the joint because it comes in completely, then the patient must lie on their affected side, and a small pillow should be placed under the shoulder, and the attendant should push the shoulder downwards until the bone of the socket is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	 Then direct the break to your fingers, and if there are bone fragments, it is necessary that you cut above them;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	 and remove the fragments gently, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, strike it at one of the incisions you have made.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	 But place this instrument under the limb to support it;
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	 and resemble a spoon, not concave, and be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	 and have two handles, as you see, with one wide and the other narrow, as the wound of the injury that you made when treating the bone.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 And when you are sure of the abscess being hot, if it opens, and if the wound is small, or you doubt the abscess being hot, then apply cloths and bandages to the wound, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	If abscess heating comes, wet linen in rose oil and asafoetida and vinegar, then place on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	 The splinting of the bone when it feels painful and has wounds or cuts, is that you put a bandage made from milled powder and egg yolk over the bone, place light strips on top, and put a sphere under it if needed.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	 Then take a very wide bandage of one palm's width, then place two cloths on top of the strips, and apply it.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	 Then take a narrow strip of three feet long and wide, and wrap it around the bandage so that the end of the bandage hangs out.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	 And place the steel upon the breakage, and turn the bendil above the neck, and beneath the saddle healthy, and beneath the saddle sick.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	 And reset from each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the breakage well, and clearly see that the steel does not move above the broken bone, if it moves, then hold it every day, and when the ligature slackens, constrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	 And make the patient lie on his back, and place him when he sleeps a small pillow under the saddle, to lift the shoulder.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	 If you align the breakage with the forceps using the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck and do not untie it except for a bad accident occurring, up to 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	 Continue the traction, if you see that it is necessary, and hold it and let it stay in place until it is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 And it is restored within 28 days, and in less to some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	 It rarely happens that a broken or dislocated shoulder heals by itself, and it should not be left without treatment but touched.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	 The armature is prepared according to the shape of the fracture, and it is reset according to its natural form in all ways that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	 Then put on the place powder from a mill with egg and soften gently, and cover it with two cloths.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	 Then place a large and fine pillow under it, a little larger than the shoulder, and if there is any hollow space under the pillow in any part of the shoulder, fill it with soft linen padding so that the pillow becomes even.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	 And then bind it all with a strong great bandage, so that the limb does not move from its place, and observe the swelling every day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	 And whenever it softens, bind it, and make the limb even if it is out of its place, and have the patient lie on their side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	 and the shoulder should be restored within 20 or 25 days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 And when this number is completed, release it, and be careful because it is not the bone that moves easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone fragment protrudes in front and not below the skin, lift it up, remove the bone, and do as we have said in the fracture of the fistula to treat an abscess by heating.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the fistula
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	 The thighbone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 And when it is broken at the joint, it declines below, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of alignment, and immediately, and sometimes vomits blood, and the fracture opens in the bone broken, and he feels it all over.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	 And the restoration is that the patient lies down on their stomach, and puts the cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two sides to your hands, and carefully adjust it in all ways possible, until the figure of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	 Then lay on plasters and bandages over the thin stem of salt or another light stick, and wrap it in a cloth, and place it above the broken bone so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	 And turn the cord tightly around the back and hold it fast, and check every hour whether the bone has set, and if it softens, tighten it again.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	 and if it is necessary to undo [the bandage], due to corrosion or itchiness at the site, or pain or abscess, then hasten, undo [it], remove the plaster, and treat the area with remedies.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then reset the plaster and hold it in place until it heals.
de la brisure des costes	of a broken rib
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	 Know that the fracture of the ribs occurs only in large ones behind the back and at the chest, and do not bend only because they are slippery.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	 And it feels well to the investigation as required.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the treatment is to set the break as necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then apply a splint and tie it with a stick if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	 If the fracture of the ribs is inclined downwards, it causes the patient great pain and shortness of breath, like in pleurisy, for the bone pierces the covering.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	 And it pushes at the tips, and immediately and vomits a large amount of blood, which is a serious illness, and the ancients have put great effort into treating it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push the break outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not let hot poultices come, unless they have arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	If they have arrived, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	 And they said that one should put bellows on the wound to suck out pus, which seems reasonable.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	 Always, there is doubt about whether the ventouse (something like a cupping glass) will draw out superfluidities to the place due to its weak positioning.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that someone should cover the wound with damp linen soaked in hot oil and put bandages between the ribs to even out the swelling around it; then it should be treated with the treatment for pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	 If the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone which does not break the cloth, and doubt exists for the patient, then it is necessary to cut through the place of the broken rib and put an instrument under it to hold it in place.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then it is necessary to cut the bone and draw gently, and afterwards sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat with plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	 If an abscess has come up, place damp cloths soaked in rose oil on top of it.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And apply the remedy to the shoulder that needs an abscess, and let it lie on its side facing the affected area until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	 Sometimes there is a fracture of the neck of the bone, and it may bend.
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	 And likewise to the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when it happens to anyone, and you wish to know if it will heal or not, take notice if the hands become softened, swollen and dead, and he cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is mortal in various positions, and if the joint does not move or feel when stretched or pricked, know that the bone joint is saved, and the patient should be cured, if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	 If it appears as though the spine in the back is fractured and you wish to know whether it is healed or not, watch if the bones are softened and if there are accidents that are in hands, and if the back jumps with involuntary movement.
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And when it is laid on its stomach, it jumps involuntarily.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when it is brought onto its stomach and it wants to lie down, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	 It means fatal.
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Do not labor at all in the treatment [of the dislocation].
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this incident does not happen to him, it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	 And the treatment is that you reward it if there is an abscess hot, placing on it oil of rose or oil from egg yolk until it is calmed;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	 then place upon one of the soothing and drying plasters and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	 and do not sleep on the part where there is pain, until it heals.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	 And if any bone should dislocate, then cover it with wax.
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Remove the bone, then close the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with stitches, then treat it with healing salve, until it heals.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	 And if the shoulder blade (the "shoulder of the cow") is broken, you push your left thumb against it and hold it even with the other hand as much as possible, then apply a splint and a wooden stick, if necessary.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 Next, you pull it together, and if there is bone protruding, raise it up, remove the bone, and heal the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the ankle bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	 It rarely happens that the shin bone is broken, and if it does happen, there is only a slight reduction in the head.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	 And it is made long, bent into a curve, and applied to the painful place where it breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	 And the resetting is such that you extend your hand over it, as long as you are above the break;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	 and learn what is the break and its shape.
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	 and if the break is only at the head, set the break equally, until it is of natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is along the length or it bends inward, make the patient lie on his stomach so that the healing of the break comes to your attention.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	 And when you have set it equally, place the splint on it, then place a rod or wedge above it and hold the break so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	 and apply the limb beneath the ribs, until the alignment is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to lie on his healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	 And if an abscess swells up there, do not touch it, until the swelling subsides, and place what we have said before on it.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	 And then return to restoration, hold it as necessary, if there is no adverse event.
et c’est li maniere.	 This is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	 The joint (adjuntoire) is between the neck and shoulder of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it must be restored according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	 One method is that you take a thick paste (fust) filled with larger grain, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	 Tie the joints with two strings, and place them on top, and hold the patient on the chair.
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	 Then throw the broken arm over the paste, until it slips out, and have a mound of paste in the middle, then place something heavy or the assistant extends it downstream.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	 Then place the mirrors in equal position to each other at the patient's hands, until the breaker returns as needed.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that you lay the patient on his bed, tie one end of the rod to his neck and command two assistants that one holds the part above the fracture with their hands, and the other holds both ends of the rod, each pulling in their respective directions.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you see that the extraction is stronger, hold the ligament beneath the break and above the break, and extend each of the attendants to their respective parts.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	 And if the breaker is near the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put a splint underneath the joint, and the other one towards the side, under the break.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	 And similarly, if the breaker is towards the side, it is necessary to place a splint lightly, without labor, so that the breaker is even on the joint and on the side.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 Then make the break equal, as needed, and hold it steady if an abscess does not come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	 And if an abscess comes out, do not hold it back for more than 7 days, put wool soaked in oil on it and let it be until the abscess is calm.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	 Then hold, and the method of holding is that you place the arm on the dislocation, then assemble the shoulder to the body, and put your hand on the shoulder or the chest.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	 and put the cloth, hold on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in place, unless something prevents it, or the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	 And if you doubt that the bone is moving, use splints, and place a larger and stronger splint than the others on the dislocation, and have space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes the dislocation 3 fingers on each side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	 Then hold firmly on the joints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter about breaking, more strongly and less in moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	 And if you see the position of the joints and the tying, as we have said, during the time that you are restoring the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess is hot, leave it to heal for seven days, as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 Then look every three days at the suture, to see if pus does not swell or appear in the place, or that the scabs do not come too close to the limb.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If the direction, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	 And if no such accidents occur, do not remove the sutures before three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back and have his hands on his stomach.
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	 And put a bandage of evenly-spun linen under the shoulder, and look at every hour of the day or night that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or the tendons are not softened.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	 if the advice is by the virtue of medicine, and he is given the meat that we have prepared before, in such a manner that the meat is first made tender.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 and when it begins to heal, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	 And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be healed within 40 days of everything.
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 Then you must loosen it and administer baths and medicines made from camphor to direct the healing.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the structure is deformed and swollen, it remains to dissolve (or loosen) for days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	on the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	 The arm is composed of two bones, which are called "fosciles," one of which is small and it is the one that follows the elbow.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	 And the others are large, and it is this one that is under, towards the little hole.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	 By chance, only the large fossa (a cavity or socket-like structure in the body) is broken, or both the large and small ones together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	 When the small fossae are broken, the restorations (the act of returning to its original position) and healings are easy.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 And when only the large one is broken, the healing is difficult and more painful than when they break together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is only the small fissure that is broken, it should be slightly stretched and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	 If it is the large fossa, it must be pulled more strongly.
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	 And extend it on the bone, grasp the hand pocket higher than the others, and let the small ones be lower than the others, and let the patient cross himself over it, and the bone should be in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any pain.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 Then extend the minister's arm to the part below his hand, or to the elbow, and another minister at the other end above it.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then equalize the shoulder, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is no dislocation that pricks the bone, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut off and remove the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	 And regarding breaking into a wound, I have spoken about it in the singular chapter.
si pren la cure.	 take care (of the wound)
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	 If, at the beginning of restoration, abscesses appear, apply the dressing made of rose oil and white beeswax, neither too hard nor too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 and securely attach (the dressing) above it subtly until the abscesses are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	 And then remove the beeswax, and apply the poultice of the mill powder with egg white, then place the hot irons, and let the iron from the wound be stronger and slightly larger than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	 And know that he must have six ribs or arms in multiple positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	 either the break is in one bone, or in two.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	 and hold the break higher than other parts, and less when pulling it apart, as I said at the beginning of the chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	 let the bandages that are above the break be soft and moist, not hard or rough.
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 let the thread, with which it is bound, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And keep the limb and the joint immobilized for some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	 and if any bad incident occurs in the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must irrigate the limb with hot water until the itching is alleviated.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And let the limb not be tightly rested.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 Then resume the immobilization, and if the joints are weakened and the bones dislocated, as in similar cases, advise accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the urine cannot reach the member due to it being too narrow, then you must soften it with oil for a few days, until the urine passes through, and then tighten it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of these things that we have mentioned happen to the patient, do not discharge them for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	 Wrap his hands around his neck and ensure that his neck is even. Watch for movement and displacement. Let him sleep on his back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 And know that this break is restored in thirty or thirty-five days, and by chance in twenty days, according to the mixtures and complexions of the properties.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	For at the back of the hand and the fingers, there are few fractures, but it occurs repeatedly many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	 And when the hand's plant is broken or bent, the patient should cross his legs and sit straight in front of him evenly.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	 Then place the hand on a cloth and extend the broken bones, aligning them with mirrors until they are well joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	 Apply the poultice and compresses, if there is no abscess present, then place a probe according to the size of the wound.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	 And let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	 If the breakage is at the front end of the limb near the belly of the plant, make a splint from cloth, and instruct the patient to bind it to his broken limb.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	 Then bind it with a long strip of cloth, and let the splint be as thick as the palm of the hand, and bind it as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the edge, you must place a splint above and another beneath in the sole, so that the hand is open and straight; then tie it all around the hand and stop the flow of blood between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	 If the breakage comes in any of the fingers, if they are bent, make it straight as necessary;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	 and bind with the palm, and if you see that it is set, place a small straight splint to lift the breakage, and do not move it.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	 And if the break is at another joint, like in the index or one of the others, align it, and place the healthy bone that is next to it.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	 Tie them all together tightly, as in a bundle, or place a splint over them, like a thong.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	 And be careful in the treatment and placement of the abscess heat, and heal what comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken leg
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	 The leg bone is often broken, and one sees this when it twists forward or backward;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	 and the treatment is that one ties a splint above the break, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	 The patient lies on their face, then each minister extends their linen equally to their part;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	 And this is when a fracture occurs in the bone.
