Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the fracture is close to the root of the shinbone, it is one of the ligaments towards the joint, and the other ligaments on the side of the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	 If it is near the knee joint, then dislocate the ligaments from the knee and extend it downwards.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 Then place the mirror on the bone equal to two hands, in accordance with its natural shape, and then apply the plaster and the strap, if no abscess comes.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	 If there is an abscess hot, let it heal first then return to your work and treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	 The binding is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	 You must wrap over the fracture in thick double bandages and remove any excess, then turn the leg until the heels come to the root of the neck, and insert a long thread between the calf and the leg, under the knee, and bring the head of the thread above.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	 Then turn the leg and thigh together, then place the splitter on the fracture, and put an arrow on the bone of the leg.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	 Use fabric of soft linen between the leg and thigh to even out the fracture, then begin to bind it firmly 3 or 4 times on the splitter.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	 and as you go up above the splitter, gradually release the pressure.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	 then pull the two ends of the thread you inserted between the leg and thigh, tie three splints above them, then go back down to the base of the thread, pulling it until the knot is loose.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 hold it in place so that it does not move from its position, then leave it as is, ensuring no abscess or inflammation or other similar problem develops.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	 And if it happens, dislocate it, and direct that which comes out, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	 and if there are bone fragments that prick (or protrude), they should be cut off if possible.
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	 and if not, it must be broken and the humour drawn out.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	 and heal as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	 Sometimes the thigh is broken so that splints are put on it, as in the shoulder or arm.
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	 Nevertheless, such a restoration does not always please the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored within a few days, either less or more, according to the various complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the street of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the groin region, there is little fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 If it breaks, it is not so much a fracture, but rather a crack or perforation, and it causes all kinds of pain and injury, and this is felt very much.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	 And the restoration is that which equalizes the limb to its opposite, until it is assembled as much as possible.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	 Then put the splint, and if needed, place a round stud, and hold it as necessary, then check all the arrangements that we have mentioned in other breakages, such as an abscess or something similar.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then apply whatever is needed to each case until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	 Know that there are two bones in the leg, of which one is correctly called "hammer", and the others are called "tarsus".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 And it happens just as with a break in the arm, and for that reason the restoration is the same as for the arm, and the treatment is the same. If the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	 And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it can be seen well.
et torne desoz.	 and turns beneath.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	 Then apply extension, make it even, and tie the joints equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	 However, if the fracture is ugly and there are many pieces, the extension should be less and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 align it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	 And when you have completed your work, take two pieces of yew wood that will splint the leg from one side to the other, and be as long as the leg from the knee down to beneath;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	 then wrap them in two layers and bind them above and below, and tie them in the middle so that the leg will not decline to the right or the left, and thus it is good.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	 And they do not administer any berse to the long part of the leg, and it is supported, and the leg is placed for restraint from movement, and properly made is what they do at the fracture or injury.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	 And move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess hot or other accident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones from the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but there may be fracture of the bones in the foot and toes, and it has no cure except for compression in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	 If it happens at the foot of the fracture, and you see these bones rise against each other, then place the patient's foot on the ground as if he is walking, and then put your foot now on his, where the bones are raised, and press until they return to their places.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	 Then place the pillow and stopper on top, and put below it the stomach of a sheep with a small table for two flat bones, then pull it towards the pelvis, then when you have wrapped cloths around, and other things that you may need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, remove the splint, because you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	 And if any of the two are broken, restore them as we have said for the hand bones.
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	 Then place a splint on the broken bone according to the length of the bone and it should be slightly larger, then put below it the table I mentioned and pull it towards the pelvis.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	 And if there are two or three, or more broken bones, place a splint on each bone according to its quantity, wrapped in one linen cloth and pull the table below the pelvis.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	 And let it be standing on top of the tablecloth with the belly facing up, so that it can be treated well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	 And you must not forget the other things that I have said about broken bones, when we have spoken of them;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	 Treat each case as required.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the wrist bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	 When the bone of the female body is broken, make her sit upright, then incline her to the lower back and hold her from behind.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	 Then fill the hollow of the patient with cotton and put as much as necessary in it.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	 Then straighten the woman, and pull the lower back gently, then push the cotton until it comes to the opening of the bone, and the broken end returns with the cotton.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	 And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and do this for 7 days or more.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	 The break will be healed, and if you see, take a bladder of a sheep, attach it to the wound opening with a string, and push the entire bladder into the bone.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	 Blow into the hollow of the neck until the bladder is full within.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	 The nature will heal the break.
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then fill it with cotton and leave it like that for some days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	 And when the bone of the arm is broken, either in a man or woman, restore it as we have said in the thighbone.
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And these breaks should not be hidden from those who study and practice this art; read my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	 For breaks indicate in many ways the right way of restoration:
enten le donques.	 Therefore, let us proceed.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	 In a spear, when it is broken, take an owl's gullet and insert the spear into it.
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	 Then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for 3 days or more, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	with break (or fracture) and wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For that person who has a fracture with a wound (or break with wound), especially if it is large as the leg bone or shoulder blade or similar, it should be cauterized now, as the cauteries that we have mentioned bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, it should be sealed with vitriol (a disinfectant), if you have no other option, then begin to restore the fracture in that same hour, or on that day, unless abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess bursts, allow the healing to continue until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is appeased; do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you will cause a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks open in the hollow of the cavity, you must set it gently and slightly extend it.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	 And if the dislocation does not appear to be set correctly for you to put it back into place with your hands, then align it with this instrument that is made of iron, which is 7 or 8 inches long, and the width is according to the size of the wound.
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	 and therefore it is necessary for the surgeon to take 3 or 4 fingers, according to what is needed in each breakage treatment.
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	 and be round and slightly larger than a thumb, so that it does not bend during the compression on the member for your work, and be sharp in front, and large in the middle towards the wound.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	 And it is called "palancha," because the curved shoulder should be placed on top of the prominent bone (of the skull).
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 and press it once, until it returns to its place, and that it is even on both sides.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 If the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot grasp the bone well, then cut the head of the bone so that the instrument can take hold.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	 And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, strike it with an appropriate tool, either a chisel or a saw, to your ability.
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	 Then remove what remains in the bone with sharpness and small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	 Make it return to its place, then moisten the cloth in black stiff vinegar and, if it is in summer, let it be clean.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	 and do not put any greased cloth or other thing on the wound that may cause rot and corruption.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	 Then apply the splints when you have set the bone, and leave the wound open, and cover it all around, according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not tightened with the fracture.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	 And many times have fools done this, and have brought harm to the patient or death or sometimes corruption.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 and the binding should be softer and more flexible than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	 If the wound is bad or large and you doubt that a bad accident may come about, as we have said, and you feel pain at the place, do not put splints on it.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 But wrap it around instead of splints, with hard cloth, and tie it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And after a day or two, if you see pus boiling at the wound, take away what you have put on it and put healing ointment on it, such as tetraformulation and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limbs should be prepared in such a way that the splints slide downwards gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they pass many days without healing and continue to swell again, know that there are small bone fragments; therefore, you must carefully open the wound and remove all the dislocated fragments causing the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula comes to the site, or any other kind of corruption, you must treat it, as he said in the chapter before this one.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	 And when the bone is broken and opened above a limb, such as the bone of the leg or shoulder, do not treat it at once, for many times death comes, but let it be until it can heal.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	 perhaps it heals by itself after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 and if you cannot, let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	broken bones that come on the suture (joint)
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	 Often health comes after the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a terrible sight to see the appearance of the limb.
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	 And perhaps the limbs cannot perform their natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	 Therefore be careful, lest we perish.
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	 administer stiffening medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, sarcocolle, acacia, and similar substances, so that you take any one of these things or all together, and grind them with a stiffening wine or with egg white or oil.
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	 And place it on the neck in a poultice, hold it tightly, and do not remove it for many days.
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	 Then dislocate [the shoulder], and start again until the nodes are removed.
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	 or hold it with a well-made piece of wood.
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	 for the property of wood is that it removes all swellings on the limbs.
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	 and if the nodes have hardened like a stone and must be removed, hit it with a blow, making the excess appear.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 or you scrape [the hardened area] with any sharp object until it is removed, and cure it until it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the limb that is weak after treatment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	 When the fracture of the bone has healed, and the limbs remain weak and fragile after it, this happens for many reasons.
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	 Because one [limb] was tied too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	 because there were too many bindings, and the nutrients could not reach the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	 When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to dryness, it cannot be put back in its place without pain.
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	 For too great movements, do not rush hourly;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	 For because he has little blood in his body, he is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	 And the remedy is to make the patient eat and make his body stretch out, until his blood is increased in him;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	 and administer baths, and give joy and pleasure;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	 Then apply tar to the member, so that the tar attracts great heat and causes it to often swell with hot water, until the heat goes to the member;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	 and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	 When the limb is twisted after restoration and the bone is broken open, and the shape of the limb is deformed, yet it does not lose its natural function;
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	 Do not believe the foolish who say that a limb must be broken anew, and many fools have done so in our land.
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	 and this procedure is blamed, and great harm comes of it, and possibly death by chance.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	 Nevertheless, if the swelling and tortures are fresh, they should be aroused with hot water, or softening herbs such as comfrey leaves, roots, and medlots, and similar things.
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	 and you make a mollifying plaster, as dayquillon often does, and take the comfrey oil and mix it with bear's grease or camomile oil, and apply the plaster.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	 You take ripe figs that are oily, grind them with wheat bran, and similar medicines that alleviate pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes, the dislocation is opened by continuous and prolonged rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 Bring movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	 If the spasm is aggravated and hardened, like stone, and iron treatment is required, it must be cauterized to the bone, cutting incision gently with a sharp instrument.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	 And apply bandages and study in its care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	If dislocation occurs in anyone, it must now be repositioned with care.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	 For if delayed, the wound swells, and perhaps it is reset improperly.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	 Therefore, it must not be moved when it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	 Many times brings spasms and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	 In any case, when it happens, make the patient purge, then leave him, until all abscesses are healed.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 Then immerse the limb in warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and heal each member as healing arrives at its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of shoulder dislocations from head to feet.
des mandibules	of jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	 The dislocation of the jaws sometimes happens in two ways, and the dislocations of both are according to two methods:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	 or they are somewhat dislocated from their places, and softened a little.
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	 When they are completely dislocated and hang downwards, and the spittle from the mouth drips uncontrollably that it cannot be held, nor can the mouth be closed, and it wraps its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it can return in various positions more often.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	 And if it is complete and entire, you must reset it immediately, without delaying;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	 And in such a way that the minister grasps the patient's head, and presses the fingers of one hand into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is on two sides;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	 And the other hand must be spread apart, to place evenly;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 Instruct the patient to soften, his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And bring the thumb equal, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	 If it is dislocated again, then exactly if both jaws are dislocated together, anoint them with hot water and oil, until they are reset gently.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	 Do not be hasty in re-setting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	 And when they are reset evenly and the patient's mouth is closed well, soften a round cloth made of rose oil and wax, then tie it lightly with many threads.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	 The patient with the illness should lie on their back, and their shoulders should be between two pillows, so that they neither move to the right nor left nor exert themselves at all, but take light meat until the pains are removed, and the jaws are fastened.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 and then eat lightly whatever they want, and do not strain at all to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaws are well fastened and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be reset in an hour and are not returned to their place, fever and usual sweats occur, and perhaps abdominal swelling, and possibly vomiting bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	 And when you see this, know that it is a loss;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	 and many times he who experiences this dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the collarbone   (metaphorical usage, meaning "neck" or "throat")
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The splint cannot dislocate from the side within the ribcage and is dislocated outside once at the hip, and it is felt clearly.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	 The treatment is that the patient lies supine on their back, and extends their arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	 And then press the joint firmly with your palm, and it will return.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	 Then place the splint and bind it tightly.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	 The shoulder that is towards the back cannot dislocate.
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	 If not, and if it dislocates at any time, then reset it to its place, as we have said.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then place the splint and bind it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until he is well.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And likewise, the shoulders of the back are returned when they are dislocated from their place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	 Know that the back is not dislocated except in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	 The first is when it dislocates at the part of the shoulder below.
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	 And the second one is at the lower part [of the body].
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	 And sometimes it dislocates in the upper part, and this happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	 It does not dislocate behind because of the shoulder blade, nor inside because of the nerves;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	 And many times it dislocates downward towards the anus, especially in those who have little flesh, because it leaps there quickly;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 In those with enough flesh, it leaps to a small extent, and returns to its place with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	Sometimes happens to some men percussion or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	 Therefore, you must test it, until you are certain.
et adonques encomence la cure.	 And then you may begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	 It is known that dislocation occurs when it moves downward towards the anus, and you must distinguish between a diseased shoulder and a healthy one, and you will find clear difference between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	 And you will find a hollow in the neck of the shoulder, and press down on it with the thumb at the base of the neck of the shoulder, just as if it were an eye.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	 The patient cannot return his hand to its normal position, nor can he make any movements.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	 And if it is dislocated upward, it should not be concealed, for you can feel it clearly with your thumb.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And this type of dislocation is not difficult to reset when it is new, or if the child is healthy.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	 The method is that the minister raises the patient's hand above, then places his hands under it, and forces the joint back into place at its proper location.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	 And the minister lifts the hand, and extends it upwards, then places it below.
si venra hastanment.	 It will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	 And if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water.
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	 And it is given a soothing and calming ointment, like a concoction of elder and fenugreek and melilot in water, and should be applied.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	 Then the patient should be made to lie on his back, and a piece of cloth equal in size, not too soft nor too hard, is placed under the shoulder. Then the physician places his foot on the cloth, lifts the head of the shoulder carefully, and pulls the hand of the patient.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	 And another servant binds the head of the patient, so that it does not move downward;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	 That shoulder comes back immediately, and if you see it like this, reset it in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	 and it is that you make a larger person be present;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	 and he should be on the right side facing the shoulder of the patient, push his shoulder down under the patient's armpit, and lift the armpit upwards so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 and another servant pulls the hand of the patient down towards his stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too lightweight, he cannot hold anything heavy, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	 And it can also be reset in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	 and it is that one sticks a long needle in the ground, so that the head should be as round as a pea, and not too thick nor too thin.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	 Then let the patient lie down under [the practitioner], but with soft fabric beneath, and the patient should be long on the bed.
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	 Extend the hand below, forming it in another way, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	 And if it does not return with all these things that we have said, do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 Take a torch from the second arm that is four feet long and three inches wide, with the head round for movement to enter fully beneath the assele in this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	 Then place the staff head on fabric soft beneath, so that the staff does not hurt the patient, then put it under the patient's assele.
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	 Extend the arm over the long staff, place the shoulder on the staff, and hold the hand at the end of the arm, then extend the other hand below, and let the body hang from another side.
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	 The joint has come back now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is inside, no matter how, you must put a sphere of cotton equal in size under the anus, then place a plaster filled with powder from the mill, along with incense and egg yolk, all over the shoulder and around; then hold it down beneath the anus, turn the string around the plaster, and bind the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	 And it is necessary that he eat little, until the limb is comforted, for it will heal faster.
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	 and then eat more after five or seven days, and move it.
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	 if it is closed and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is dislocated due to moisture or for another reason, you should administer fire cauterization at three places as stated in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	 And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift its arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened.
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	 And understand that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	 Dislocations that are towards the hip and the buttocks, or behind, are made by impact and extension of hands, and another treatment is applied.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And heal until he is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after the healing, if there is still pain in the limb and slow movement, the patient should use baths several times until the pain subsides and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation cost   (This line seems incomplete, as it does not seem to follow the pattern of translation from the previous lines.)
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	 Know that the shoulder joint has been dislocated at points, and at points it returns.
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	 And it has been dislocated in all parts, both front and back, and the dislocation is not put back in place, since it can be seen clearly and felt.
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	 It dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when joining the broken bone with the healthy one, make sure it can be seen clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the dislocated joint cannot bend the arm nor touch the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	 You must reset it accordingly when an abscess arrives at the shoulder, because if an abscess comes to the shoulder, it would be difficult to reset.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	 And in case it cannot be completely returned from all sides, especially when it is at the back.
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	 It is worse than other dislocations and causes more pain, and in case there comes death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	 And the restoration is, when it can be brought back to such a state, that you extend your hand to both hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	 and the arms should be spread out, and the hands in line with the mirror on both sides, above and below, and push the joint back to its places together, or at the root of the palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it will return when you fold your hand over your other hand, and push against the bone joint that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	 And if it does not return to its place, then administer strong traction;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	 and that two attendants extend the arm and pull it, and then one of them holds it still while the other pulls on it so that it does not move during traction.
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	 Then turn the arm from each side, then when you have wrapped a double cloth long and wide around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	 And when the healer joins the joint to his hand, he pushes it away with some oil to soften the joint, then forces the joint back into place until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 When it is in place, he puts some plaster dry with egg white on it and pulls it straight, then ties the arm around the patient's neck and leaves it for several days, then unties it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	 And if the joint is held firmly in place, he unties the tie and leaves it be.
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	 If you see that the joint does not hold well, repeat the plaster and the tie and leave it in that state for several days until it is firmly set.
puis le deslie.	 Then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	 And if it feels sore after the resetting of the joint and it stiffens, bathe and rub it well, and press until it is soothed.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	 And place a sheep's bladder on the joint, then let it stay for a day and a night, then remove it, and let him enter into water.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	 And when it bleeds, rub the joint gently, then place the bladder back on, and then enter into water again.
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And do this two or three times until it is healed.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	 And if you see, place a warm wet cloth with butter on it and hold it there.
si revenra a sa disposition.	 It will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	 The joint of the hand is dislocated, and when it returns, it is easy, more than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	 Immediately, it must be returned to its place quickly, during the very moment when it is dislocated, unless the joint is swollen or there is an abscess hot.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	 And the repositioning is that you place the affected hand on a table, extend the fingers, and align them, so that the palm is over the appearance of the joint, and push until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	 Then, you must look if it is in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 Then, the patient places the back of his hand on a table for extension and repositioning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, place the patient's dorsal side of his hand on the table, and hold your hand over that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	 If it returns now, it is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If not, strain it with plasters to calm the abscess and leave it so to start healing.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	 And if it cannot endure, and you cannot put it back in place after any days, then the dislocation remains twisted.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	 The patient must not exert the hand for as long as it is paralyzed, and cannot strain anything completely.
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	 Therefore know that nerves or arteries are cut.
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 There is no other remedy except to strain it by fire cautery in the case, and perhaps nothing else works.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is at its place, put a splint on it as we have said, then bind and leave for 5 days, then unbind and leave in this manner.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it cannot be moved well and there is no pain, moist with warm water and rub until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers on the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	 The fingers are dislocated on both sides of the hand at times, or at the back of the palm or the belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	 Then place the fingers, and push the dislocation back towards your fingertips until it returns, then hold the finger's head, and bend it towards the part where it is disjoint.
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	 And let him wait [the shoulder] for two days, and then make it even on that day;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	 And bind it up as we have said, and loosen it for a day, and make it move, and then bind it again.
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated at the elbow of the arm, and do as you have done before, until it is healed.
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 And do the same when it is dislocated from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	And for the dislocation of the small of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the small of the back or neck is dislocated, and there are many such dislocations without a cure, death quickly approaches the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	 And the signs are that the joints jump involuntarily, and they cannot be held, and many times a limb is softened, whether it is the two knees or the two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	 And often the sciatic nerve becomes paralyzed at four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	 that which becomes paralyzed in the back is called "gilbositez";
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	 the treatment is that you should look to see if the gilbositez has come from childhood;
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 if there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	 And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient methods of cure used to say in great words, but it is not at all useful in every case.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 but I have condensed it according to my intention and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	 I say that in the gilbosite that comes before the worst case, there is no remedy or health;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	 And likewise the one that comes straight towards the two sides, cannot be cured by others except by him who comes from behind, as I said;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	 and the patient should be stretched out on his face in an even position, and there should be pressure underneath him so that he does not bleed.
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	 then thrust the needle into the head of the shoulder in the earth and the other at the joints, and tie a rope under the patient's shoulders, and one around his thighs, and at the knees, and at the ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	 and two assistants know the ropes, one at the head and the others at the joints, between the two needles.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 and let the needles be well closed as we have said, and the mirrors place their palms on the spine in form, until it recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	 And if the dislocation does not return with this treatment, take a board three feet long and bend it so that its top is underneath, and have the patient lie on their side, and push the end of the board underneath the opening, then place the middle part of the board on the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	 And press the mirrors' feet on the other end of the board and hold firmly until it returns to its place.
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 If you see that it does not return, turn the patient to the opposite side.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	 And you should insert two fingers of a hand's breadth into the head of the patient and between them leave a palm's space in length.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	 And each finger should be held still, or the patient should be turned as needed, and the fingers should be firmly pressed into the ground so they do not move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	 And between each two sparks let there be a spark turning, as the links turn, and have in turning two small sparks of one span long, to turn the turning.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 Then tie the link that is between the ankles to the upper turning and the other link towards the feet to the lower turning, and each of the servants turns his turning along the entire length, and the master puts the splint equal as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And when it is equalized, place a plaster with drying agent and egg on top of it, then bandage it, then place the cast from a tabletop of three feet long, which presses against the swelling and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a rope as we have said, and use the patient with subtle nursing until he is healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	 If anything comes at the end of health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the steam that we have said before.
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	 Sometimes they administer a wooden piece, and sometimes the appearance comes in the back of the spine, and it is thought to be dislocation.
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	 It is the bone that opens, which means there should be no presumption about it.
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 By chance death may come.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the dislocations of the shoulder
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	 Note that the junctions of the neck and shoulder do not come violently except for dislocation only, they do not break in the same way as other joints.
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	 The junction of the neck is dislocated in four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	 Inside and out, front and back;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	 Also inside thereafter, but slightly less so outside in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	 And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when the sick leg is joined with the healthy one, it is longer and wider apart, and the sick person's thigh is less flexible than the healthy one, and they cannot bend their knee in fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 and it is the loosened joint that swells with abscess hot, because the hips of the thigh come there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that one who suffers from this condition is that this event happens contrary to what was mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	 And the signs of him who has it in front are that his leg is well aligned according to the completion;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	 However, it does not bend the knee without pain, and if you want to make him walk, he cannot do so, and he holds his urine, and his ankle swells up, and when he walks, he limps on his heels.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that one whose condition is at the back, are that he cannot extend his knee nor bend it double, and this leg is twisted more than the other, and the ankle becomes softened, and the head of the thighbone is beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	 The re-alignments of this type of dislocation are such that you check if the dislocation is old and remains according to its position, without any treatment.
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	 it should not be assumed that there is treatment required.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	 And for the one in whom the dislocation is fresh, and it is of four types of dislocation, hasten that you turn the joint, push it inward and outward, and move it left and right;
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	 In case it returns, no further treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	 And if it does not return in this manner, you must apply a strong force and push the leg firmly with two hands or to the thigh that is tied above the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	 And another minister extends his hand over in such a way that he pushes his hands beneath the buttocks, then binds it with a soft rope around the thigh.
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	 and another ties the head with the rope.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 They stretch upward and downward all at once, so that the patient is raised from the ground once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to the four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	 If this does not happen, it is necessary to treat his condition.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	 When the dislocation is at the back, you must have the patient lie on his healthy side, then place the rope around the root of the thigh, and the affected area below the groin, then pull the rope towards the groin, and towards the shoulder.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	 Then take another assistant's hands, and embrace the large thigh of the ill leg, and stretch it out in a wide form.
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	 then return to its place now.
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 and this method of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	 And if you cannot hold it in this manner as we have said, then you must bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong rope above the heels and knees, and the ill leg should be extended two fingers more than others.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	 then it should be hung from a post by its head with its arms hanging long.
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 then command the assistant to embrace the thigh and another assistant should be hanging with the patient who embraces the thigh, because the joints are returning quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	 And when the dislocation is out of place, the patient lies down, as we have said in the one who has dislocated his shoulder; and stretches the ligament above the sick leg properly, and also above the pelvis.
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	 then place two splinters, one at the head and another at the feet; then insert the splinter between the patient's knees in the shape.
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 and have soaked cloths in warm water around it to prevent the patient from bleeding; then each attendant extends towards him, and the one who mirrors puts his hand equal to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns [to its place], that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, put it on a table and press as we have said in the gout, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	 And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the sick leg immediately, and as I have said.
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	 And set the mirrors his pain on top of the angry sickness, then press with the other hand and stretch it towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	 And if the dislocation is to the outside, it should not be stretched downwards, nor raised up towards the ground, but rather as if the hip were dislocated to the outside, as we have said in the treatment of two hips.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	 and it should be on its back, and the ligament stretched as we have said before, and must be pressed on the joint at the table.
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	 and when the patient stretches out his legs, they will be even.
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	 Then align the thighs and place the bolster, and tie it with a strap so that the hip does not move.
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	 And let it rest for three days or four, then dislocate it, and place the splint on top.
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	 If you see they are even, hold them steady as before, and let it rest for three days.
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 Then dislocate it, and make it go gently, until the limb is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation in the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	 The thighbone is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	 that is to say, from within and outward, and backward.
et ne desalue point devant.	 Do not dislocate it forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	 And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if it does not bend at the knee, know that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	 And the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his chest, and put his foot on your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	 Then take his thigh with your hands, pull it between your hands, then bend both sides of the thigh together.
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	 and another servant extends his foot until the thigh returns to its place, and the sign is that he bends his leg easily at the knee.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	 and apply the plaster, then bend the leg to the thigh, and keep them bound tightly for three or four days, then release it.
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And do not let the patient walk, until the limbs are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not straight, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of dislocation, until it is sound.
de la dislocation dou talon	about the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes swollen, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	 The sign is that the ankle is swollen, and it tends to move towards the part where it has been dislocated.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 The reduction (of the dislocation) is easy, and it should be extended slightly when only stretched out.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	 And when it is completely dislocated, you must make the patient sit upright, and hold him by the leg, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	 then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, then with your left hand twice, then raise it up and push the foot up hard;
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	 and do this twice as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot;
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	 if it goes back into place, that is good;
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	 but if not, continue the work, for it will come back again;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	 and if it cannot go back in this way, lay the patient on his back on the ground, and drive the passael firmly into the ground between his legs, and tie cloths around so as not to hurt the patient;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	 Then, ministers stain the thigh, and another minister extends the foot to their hands or fingers, so that it lies across the neck of the foot.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	 Then each minister extends evenly, and the clamps should be close together between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when they are stretched.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 Then, the master equalizes the dislocation in his hands, and another minister stains the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	 And when it is in place, he puts the plaster and wool on top, and he forms it, ties the foot to the leg, and guards the nerves that are above the ankle, so the clamps are not too tight.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	 Leave it [the dislocation] for two or three days, and if it gets worse [i.e., the shoulder slips out again], hold it steady.
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	 Release it [the dislocation] on the third or fourth day, and warn the patient to abstain from walking for four days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And if he goes before that term [of three to four days], it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess swells up, you must calm it as we have said elsewhere, until it is healthy.
des dois	of the two [shoulders]
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both shoulders are dislocated, they must be carefully stretched out without strain, and it is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	 If the dislocation is in any notch of the back or neck, you must have the patient sit on a flat surface [or table] straight, and place your foot on the opening of those joints, then press firmly on your foot until it returns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	 When it is level and there is no opening, place a board under the foot of your foot, then hold it firmly, and let it stay for three days, then release it.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And let him rest until he recovers.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	 When a wound occurs with dislocation and it is to be restored, often the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	 Do not be presumptuous in the treatment, if you are not skilled in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate, merciful, and patient, do not be bold.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	 And at the beginning of treating an abscess, apply a warm cautery, and let the patient be in God's hands if you see no hope of health.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	 And when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the abscess grows cold.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	 And when the limb is in place, apply warm cautery to the abscess and treat the wound as necessary with dry ointments.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	 And if there is fracture with dislocation, and small bones are displaced, if you reset the bones, do as we have said in simple diseases;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 And be careful not to enter into fear, according to what I have said, for it will increase according to your Creator, and for the wisdom of your weapon and body.
